[Orchestrator] Loaded CoW source context (26169 chars).

--- Planning Phase (Iteration 1/3) ---

[PlannerAgent] Reasoning:
The goal is to prove that for a non-empty word w (w ≠ []) and positive n (0 < n), the power w^n is non-empty. The key insight is that the length of w^n is n * w.length (by lemma Word.length_pow). Since w ≠ [] implies w.length > 0, and n > 0, the product n * w.length is strictly positive. Hence (w^n).length > 0. By the equivalence in List.length_pos_iff_ne_nil, a word has positive length exactly when it is non-empty. Therefore w^n ≠ [].

The proof can be done entirely with arithmetic and length lemmas already available in the CoW context (Word.length_pow) and Mathlib (List.length_pos_iff_ne_nil, Nat.mul_pos). No additional imported lemmas are required beyond those already present in the file header and the CoW library.

[PlannerAgent] Plan:
1. From the hypothesis `hw : w ≠ []`, deduce `hwpos : 0 < w.length` using `List.length_pos_iff_ne_nil.mpr hw`.
2. With `hn : 0 < n` and `hwpos`, obtain `hprod_pos : 0 < n * w.length` using `Nat.mul_pos hn hwpos`.
3. Using the CoW lemma `Word.length_pow w n`, rewrite `n * w.length` as `(w ^ n).length`:
   `have hlen_pow : (w ^ n).length = n * w.length := Word.length_pow w n` (or use `...` with `simpa`). Then `hprod_pos` gives `0 < (w ^ n).length` after rewriting.
4. Apply `List.length_pos_iff_ne_nil.mp` to the positive length of `w ^ n` to conclude `w ^ n ≠ []`.
   (Alternatively, use `by intro heq; rw [heq] at hlen_pow; simp at hlen_pow` to derive a contradiction.)
5. The goal is discharged.

--- Planning Phase (Iteration 2/3) ---

[PlannerAgent] Reasoning:
The previous attempt using `List.length_pos_iff_ne_nil` and `Nat.mul_pos` may have failed due to definitional subtleties with `Word.length` versus `List.length`, or because `simpa` couldn't rewrite `Word.length_pow` without it being marked `[simp]`. A simpler and more direct proof uses the structural property of `List`: if a concatenation `u ⬝ w` equals `[]`, then `w = []`. By induction on `n` (or case analysis on the positive `n`), we can apply `Word.pow_succ` to reduce to a concatenation and then use `List.append_eq_nil` to derive a contradiction with `hw`. This avoids all length arithmetic and is robust.

The case analysis: Since `hn : 0 < n`, we know `n` is not `0`, so `n` is `succ m` for some `m`. Then `w ^ (m+1) = w ^ m ⬝ w`. If this were `[]`, then `w` would be `[]`, contradicting `hw`.

[PlannerAgent] Plan:
1. Use `cases n` to split into the cases `n = 0` and `n = m.succ` for some `m : ℕ`.
   - In the `n = 0` case, we have `hn : 0 < 0`. This is impossible. Use `exact (Nat.lt_irrefl 0 hn).elim` (or `exact Nat.not_lt_zero 0 hn`). Alternatively, `exact (Nat.lt_of_lt_of_le hn hn).false.elim`? Actually `Nat.lt_irrefl 0 hn : ¬ 0 < 0`, so `exact (Nat.lt_irrefl 0 hn)` works because `hn` is a proof of `0 < 0`, and `Nat.lt_irrefl` expects a `¬ a < a`. More precisely, `Nat.lt_irrefl 0 : ¬ 0 < 0`, so `apply` gives `exact (Nat.lt_irrefl 0) hn`. Simpler: `exact Nat.lt_of_lt_of_le hn hn`. I'll use `exact (Nat.lt_irrefl 0 hn).elim`? Actually `Nat.lt_irrefl` is a lemma `¬ a < a`, not a function. Use `exact absurd hn (Nat.lt_irrefl 0)`. But easiest: `exact (by decide : ¬ 0 < 0) hn`. However, `by decide` is heavy. Use `exact Nat.not_lt_zero 0 hn`. There is lemma `Nat.not_lt_zero`. So `exact (Nat.not_lt_zero 0 hn).elim`. I'll use `Nat.not_lt_zero 0 hn` directly.
   - In the `n = m.succ` case, we need to prove `w ^ (m.succ) ≠ []`. Apply `intro h` to assume the contrary. Then use the lemma `Word.pow_succ w m` to rewrite `h : w ^ (m.succ) = w ^ m ⬝ w = []`. So `rw [Word.pow_succ w m] at h` gives `h : (w ^ m) ⬝ w = []`. Since `⬝` is definitionally `List.append`, we can apply `List.append_eq_nil.mp` to `h` to get `(h^.^1) : (w ^ m) = []` and `(h^.^2) : w = []`. Use `have hnil := (List.append_eq_nil.mp h).2` to obtain `hnil : w = []`. Then `exact hw hnil`.
2. The `Intro h` step inside the `succ` case uses `List.append_eq_nil` which is in `Mathlib.Data.List.Basic` (already imported).
3. This plan uses only `Word.pow_succ` and `List.append_eq_nil` and the standard `Nat` lemma `Nat.not_lt_zero`.

The tactic plan in pseudocode:
```lean4
cases n with
| zero => exact absurd hn (Nat.not_lt_zero 0)
| succ m =>
    intro h
    rw [Word.pow_succ w m] at h
    have hnil : w = [] := (List.append_eq_nil.mp h).2
    exact hw hnil
```
This will succeed.

[ 3/45]           Word | MEDIUM | pow_eq_nil_iff

[Orchestrator] Initiating Multi-Agent Repair for pow_eq_nil_iff
[Orchestrator] Loaded CoW source context (26169 chars).

==================================================
--- Planning Phase (Iteration 1/3) ---

[PlannerAgent] Reasoning:
The theorem states that for a word `w` and `n : ℕ`, `w ^ n = []` iff `n = 0` or `w = []`. This is a fundamental property of the free monoid. The forward direction relies on the length formula `(w ^ n).length = n * w.length` (lemma `Word.length_pow`). If `w ^ n = []`, its length is `0`, so `n * w.length = 0`. By `Nat.mul_eq_zero.mp` we get that either `n = 0` or `w.length = 0`. If `w.length = 0`, then `w = []` by `List.length_eq_zero.mp`. The reverse direction splits into two cases: if `n = 0`, then `w ^ 0 = []` by `Word.pow_zero`. If `w = []`, then `[] ^ n = []` by `Word.one_pow n` (where `one_pow` says `([] : Word α) ^ n = []`).

All necessary lemmas are already in the provided CoW context:
- `Word.length_pow w n : (w ^ n).length = n * w.length` (from Word.lean)
- `List.length_eq_zero` (from Mathlib Data.List.Basic, gives `w.length = 0 ↔ w = []`)
- `Nat.mul_eq_zero` (from Mathlib Data.Nat.Basic)
- `Word.pow_zero w : w ^ 0 = []` (from Word.lean)
- `Word.one_pow n : ([] : Word α) ^ n = []` (from Word.lean)

[PlannerAgent] Plan:
1. **Forward direction (`→`)**:
   - Assume `h : w ^ n = []`.
   - Use the length formula: `(w ^ n).length = n * w.length` via `Word.length_pow w n`.
   - From `h`, we know `(w ^ n).length = 0` (by rewriting `h` into the `Word.length_pow` equation, or by `simpa [h]` using `Word.length_pow`).
   - So we have `hprod_zero : n * w.length = 0`.
   - Apply `Nat.mul_eq_zero.mp` to `hprod_zero` to get `hcases : n = 0 ∨ w.length = 0`.
   - Analyze the disjunction:
     * If `hn : n = 0`, then `left` with `hn`.
     * If `hwlen0 : w.length = 0`, then `hwnil : w = []` via `List.length_eq_zero.mp hwlen0`, and `right` with `hwnil`.
2. **Reverse direction (`←`)**:
   - Assume `h : n = 0 ∨ w = []`.
   - Analyze the disjunction:
     * If `hn : n = 0`, rewrite `n` to `0` using `hn`, then `w ^ 0 = []` by `Word.pow_zero w`.
     * If `hw : w = []`, rewrite `w` to `[]` using `hw`, then `[] ^ n = []` by `Word.one_pow n`.
3. The two directions together give the equivalence.

--- Planning Phase (Iteration 2/3) ---

[PlannerAgent] Reasoning:
The previous approach using length arithmetic (`Word.length_pow`, `Nat.mul_eq_zero`, `List.length_eq_zero`) might have encountered subtle definitional or import issues. A more structural proof that avoids length entirely is to use induction on `n` together with `Word.pow_succ` and `List.append_eq_nil`. The forward direction (`w ^ n = [] → n = 0 ∨ w = []`) can be proved by induction on `n`. The base case `n = 0` trivially gives `n = 0`. In the inductive step `n = m+1`, we have `w ^ (m+1) = w ^ m ⬝ w` by `Word.pow_succ`. If this equals `[]`, then by `List.append_eq_nil` we deduce both `w ^ m = []` and `w = []`. The latter immediately gives the desired conclusion. The reverse direction already uses `Word.pow_zero` and `Word.one_pow` as before. All required lemmas are explicitly present in the CoW context and are proven by `rfl` or simple arithmetic, so no hidden failures should occur.

[PlannerAgent] Plan:
1. **Forward direction (`w ^ n = [] → n = 0 ∨ w = [])`**:
   - Proceed by induction on `n`.
   - **Base case `n = 0`**: we must show `0 = 0 ∨ w = []`. This is immediate by `Or.inl rfl`.
   - **Inductive step**: assume `IH : w ^ m = [] → m = 0 ∨ w = []` for an arbitrary `m`. We need to show `w ^ (m+1) = [] → (m+1 = 0 ∨ w = [])`.
     * Introduce `h : w ^ (m+1) = []`. 
     * Rewrite using `Word.pow_succ w m` at `h`, obtaining `h' : (w ^ m) ⬝ w = []`.
     * Apply `List.append_eq_nil` to `h'`, giving a pair `⟨hmem, hw⟩` with `hmem : w ^ m = []` and `hw : w = []`.
     * Now `hw` directly gives the goal `Or.inr hw`. (The induction hypothesis is not needed.)
2. **Reverse direction (`(n = 0 ∨ w = []) → w ^ n = []`)**:
   - Introduce `h : n = 0 ∨ w = []`. 
   - Case analysis:
     * If `hn : n = 0`, substitute `hn` into the goal and use `Word.pow_zero w`.
     * If `hw : w = []`, substitute `hw` and use `Word.one_pow n` (which states `([] : Word α) ^ n = []`).

[Orchestrator] Loaded CoW source context (26169 chars).

--- Planning Phase (Iteration 1/3) ---

[PlannerAgent] Reasoning:
The goal is to show `w^m ⬝ w^n = w^n ⬝ w^m`. The CoW lemma `Word.pow_add` states `w ^ (m + n) = w ^ m ⬝ w ^ n`. Using this, both sides can be expressed as `w^(m+n)` and `w^(n+m)`, respectively. Because addition is commutative (`Nat.add_comm m n`), these two powers are identical. Therefore, the equality holds. All necessary lemmas are present in the CoW context: `Word.pow_add` (from Word.lean) and `Nat.add_comm` (from Mathlib).

[PlannerAgent] Plan:
1. Use `calc` block to rewrite both sides:
   - `w ^ m ⬝ w ^ n = w ^ (m + n)` by `(Word.pow_add w m n).symm` (or `Word.pow_add`).
   - `w ^ n ⬝ w ^ m = w ^ (n + m)` by `(Word.pow_add w n m).symm`.
   - Finally, `w ^ (m + n) = w ^ (n + m)` by `congrArg (fun k => w ^ k) (Nat.add_comm m n)` (or `rw [Nat.add_comm m n]`).
2. Combine the three equalities to obtain `w ^ m ⬝ w ^ n = w ^ n ⬝ w ^ m`.


--- Builder Execution (Attempt 1/3) ---

```lean4
  w ^ m ⬝ w ^ n = w ^ (m + n) := (Word.pow_add w m n).symm
  _ = w ^ (n + m) := by rw [Nat.add_comm m n]
  _ = w ^ n ⬝ w ^ m := Word.pow_add w n m
```

--- Planning Phase (Iteration 1/3) ---

[PlannerAgent] Reasoning:
The theorem states that powers of a non-empty word are distinct for different exponents. The proof uses the length formula: `(w^k).length = k * w.length` (lemma `Word.length_pow`). From `w^m = w^n`, we equate lengths, obtaining `m * w.length = n * w.length`. Since `w ≠ []`, its length is positive (`List.length_pos_iff_ne_nil`). Canceling the positive factor yields `m = n` via `Nat.eq_of_mul_eq_mul_right`. The steps are completely explicit and rely only on lemmas already present in the CoW context and Mathlib arithmetic.

[PlannerAgent] Plan:
1. From the hypothesis `h : w ^ m = w ^ n`, apply `Word.length` to both sides to obtain `hlen_eq : (w ^ m).length = (w ^ n).length`. (Use `have hlen_eq := congrArg Word.length h`.)
2. Using `Word.length_pow w m` and `Word.length_pow w n`, rewrite `hlen_eq` as `h_mul_eq : m * (Word.length w) = n * (Word.length w)`. (e.g., `simpa [Word.length_pow] using hlen_eq`)
3. From `hw : w ≠ []`, deduce `hpos : 0 < Word.length w` via `List.length_pos_iff_ne_nil.mpr hw`.
4. Apply `Nat.eq_of_mul_eq_mul_right hpos h_mul_eq` to conclude `m = n`.

[ 6/45]           Word | MEDIUM | pow_add_length_eq

[Orchestrator] Initiating Multi-Agent Repair for pow_add_length_eq
[Orchestrator] Loaded CoW source context (26169 chars).

==================================================
--- Planning Phase (Iteration 1/3) ---

[PlannerAgent] Reasoning:
The lemma `Word.length_pow w k` gives `(w ^ k).length = k * w.length`. Thus LHS = `(m+n) * w.length`. RHS = `m * w.length + n * w.length`. By distributivity of multiplication over addition in ℕ (`Nat.add_mul` or the `ring` tactic), they are equal. The proof can be done by rewriting with `Word.length_pow` and then applying `ring` or `Nat.add_mul`. No other lemmas are required.

[PlannerAgent] Plan:

2. Rewrite each term on the right-hand side using `Word.length_pow w m` and `Word.length_pow w n`: `(w ^ m).length + (w ^ n).length = m * w.length + n * w.length`.

4. Combining these rewrites yields the equality. A `simpa [Word.length_pow]` using `by ring` or `simpa [Word.length_pow, Nat.add_mul]` is sufficient.

[ 9/45]         Factor | MEDIUM | prefix_of_pow_succ

[Orchestrator] Initiating Multi-Agent Repair for prefix_of_pow_succ
[Orchestrator] Loaded CoW source context (26169 chars).

==================================================
--- Planning Phase (Iteration 1/3) ---

[PlannerAgent] Reasoning:
We need to prove `w ≤ₚ w ^ (n+1)`. The lemma `Word.pow_succ w n` gives `w^(n+1) = w^n ⬝ w`. This alone does not directly show `w` is a prefix, because it's at the end. However, we can prove by induction on `n` that `w` is a prefix of `w^(k+1)` for all `k`. The base case `k=0` is `w ≤ₚ w^1 = w`, true by `IsPrefix.self`. For the induction step from `k` to `k+1`, we assume `w ≤ₚ w^(k+1)`. Then `w^(k+2) = w^(k+1) ⬝ w`. Since `w ≤ₚ w^(k+1)`, we can write `w^(k+1) = w ++ x` for some `x`. Then `w^(k+1) ⬝ w = w ++ (x ++ w)`, so `w` remains a prefix. This reasoning uses the definition of prefix from `IsPrefix.def` and the associativity of list append (`List.append_assoc`). All needed lemmas are present in the CoW library.

[PlannerAgent] Plan:
1. Use induction on `n`.
   - **Base case `n = 0`**: `w ^ (0+1) = w`. The goal `w ≤ₚ w` follows from `IsPrefix.self w`. So `simp` suffices.
   - **Inductive step**: assume `IH : w ≤ₚ w ^ (k + 1)` for some `k`, prove `w ≤ₚ w ^ (k+1 + 1)`.
2. In the inductive step:
   - Rewrite the target exponent: `w ^ ((k+1)+1) = w ^ (k+1) ⬝ w` using `Word.pow_succ w (k+1)`.
   - From `IH`, obtain `x` such that `w^(k+1) = w ++ x` using `(IsPrefix.def _ _).mp`.
   - Apply `(IsPrefix.def _ _).mpr` to construct a witness for `w ≤ₚ (w^(k+1) ⬝ w)`.
   - Provide the witness `x ++ w` and prove the equality:
     `(w^(k+1)) ⬝ w = (w ++ x) ++ w = w ++ (x ++ w)`.
   - This rewriting uses `Word.concat` (changing `⬝` to `++`), the obtained equation `hx`, and `List.append_assoc`.
3. The proof is complete.


--- Builder Execution (Attempt 1/3) ---
[Orchestrator] ⚠️  Proof contains 'sorry' — treating as incomplete.

```lean4
induction n with
  | zero =>
    simp
  | succ k ih =>
    rw [Word.pow_succ w (k + 1)]
    rcases (IsPrefix.def w (w ^ (k + 1))).mp ih with ⟨x, hx⟩
    apply (IsPrefix.def w ((w ^ (k + 1)) ⬝ w)).mpr
    refine ⟨x ⬝ w, ?_⟩
    rw [hx, Word.concat, Word.concat, List.append_assoc]
```

--- Planning Phase (Iteration 1/3) ---

[PlannerAgent] Reasoning:
The statement `w ^ m ≤ₛ w ^ n` for `m ≤ n` follows from the exponent law `Word.pow_add` and the fact that `n` can be expressed as `(n - m) + m` when `m ≤ n`. Then `w^n = w^((n-m)+m) = w^(n-m) * w^m`, so `w^m` is a suffix with prefix `w^(n-m)`. The proof uses `Nat.add_sub_cancel' h` to get the decomposition and `IsSuffix.def` to exhibit the witness. All necessary lemmas are already imported.

[PlannerAgent] Plan:

2. Rewrite the goal using `h_sum` to get `w ^ m ≤ₛ w ^ (d + m)`.
3. Apply `Word.pow_add w d m` to rewrite the right-hand side as `(w ^ d) ⬝ (w ^ m)`.
4. The goal becomes `w ^ m ≤ₛ ((w ^ d) ⬝ (w ^ m))`. Now apply `(IsSuffix.def _ _).mpr` with witness `w ^ d` and the trivial equality `(w ^ d) ⬝ (w ^ m) = (w ^ d) ⬝ (w ^ m)`.
5. Conclude `w ^ m ≤ₛ w ^ n`.

In lean4 pseudocode:
```
theorem suffix_of_pow_le (w : Word α) {m n : ℕ} (h : m ≤ n) : w ^ m ≤ₛ w ^ n := by
  set d := n - m with hd
  have h_sum : n = d + m := by rw [hd, Nat.add_comm, Nat.add_sub_cancel' h]
  rw [h_sum, Word.pow_add w d m]
  exact (IsSuffix.def _ _).mpr ⟨w ^ d, rfl⟩
```
This avoids any induction and directly uses the additive decomposition of exponents.

The necessary lemmas are `Nat.sub_add_cancel`, `Word.pow_add`, and `IsSuffix.def`, all already imported.

--- Planning Phase (Iteration 1/3) ---

[PlannerAgent] Reasoning:
The statement is a classical property of words: a prefix and a suffix whose lengths sum to the length of the whole word together partition the word. Using `IsPrefix.def` and `IsSuffix.def` we obtain decompositions `w = u ++ x` and `w = y ++ v`. From these we get `u ++ x = y ++ v`. The length condition `u.length + v.length = w.length` combined with the length equations from the decompositions yields `x.length = v.length` and `u.length = y.length` (by canceling lengths). Applying `List.append_inj` with the equality of the prefix lengths gives `u = y` and `x = v`. Then `w = u ++ x = u ++ v = u ⬝ v`. All required lemmas (`List.length_append`, `List.append_inj`, `Nat.add_right_cancel`, `Nat.add_left_cancel`) are available in the imported libraries.

[PlannerAgent] Plan:
1. From `hpre : u ≤ₚ w`, obtain `x` such that `hwx : w = u ++ x` using `(IsPrefix.def u w).mp hpre`.
2. From `hsuf : v ≤ₛ w`, obtain `y` such that `hwy : w = y ++ v` using `(IsSuffix.def v w).mp hsuf`.
3. Combine to get `h_eq_cat : u ++ x = y ++ v` by rewriting `hwy` into `hwx`.
   `have h_eq_cat : u ++ x = y ++ v := by rw [← hwx, hwy]`.
4. Derive length equalities:
   - From `hwx`, we have `h_len_w : w.length = u.length + x.length` by `rw [hwx, List.length_append]`.
   - From `hwy`, we have `w.length = y.length + v.length` similarly.
   - The hypothesis `hlen` says `u.length + v.length = w.length`.
   - Using these, compute:
     `h_len_xv : x.length = v.length`:
       `have h_sum1 : u.length + x.length = u.length + v.length := by rw [← h_len_w, hlen]`
       `exact add_right_cancel h_sum1`? Actually `Nat.add_right_cancel : a + b = c + b → a = c`. So we have `u.length + x.length = u.length + v.length` → `x.length = v.length`. Use `apply` or `have := add_right_cancel ...`? More precisely `have hxlen_eq_vlen : x.length = v.length := Nat.add_right_cancel (by rw [← h_len_w, hlen]; rfl)`?
     Better to state: `have hxlen_eq_vlen : x.length = v.length := by
        have htemp : u.length + x.length = u.length + v.length := by
          rw [← h_len_w, hlen]
        exact (add_right_cancel htemp)` — but `add_right_cancel` is in `Nat`. Provide the right lemma.
   - Similarly, `h_len_uy : u.length = y.length`:
       `have htemp2 : y.length + v.length = u.length + v.length := by rw [← h_len_w', hlen]` but we need `h_len_w'` from `hwy`. Then `exact (add_left_cancel htemp2)` gives `y.length = u.length`. Actually `add_left_cancel` cancels the left addend: `a + b = a' + b → a = a'`. In `y.length + v.length = u.length + v.length`, we can cancel `v.length` using `Nat.add_right_cancel`. So we need `Nat.add_right_cancel` again. So `huylen_eq_ulen : y.length = u.length := by
         have htemp2 : y.length + v.length = u.length + v.length := by
           rw [← h_len_w_y, hlen]
         exact (Nat.add_right_cancel htemp2)` 
   We'll need to name `h_len_w_x` and `h_len_w_y`.
   Let's define:
   `have h_len_w_x : w.length = u.length + x.length := by rw [hwx, List.length_append]`
   `have h_len_w_y : w.length = y.length + v.length := by rw [hwy, List.length_append]`
   Then `have htemp1 : u.length + x.length = u.length + v.length := by rw [← h_len_w_x, hlen]`
   `have hxlen_eq_vlen : x.length = v.length := (Nat.add_right_cancel htemp1).symm?` Actually `Nat.add_right_cancel htemp1` returns `x.length = v.length` (not symmetric). It's exactly that.
   Similarly `have htemp2 : y.length + v.length = u.length + v.length := by rw [← h_len_w_y, hlen]`
   `have hylen_eq_ulen : y.length = u.length := Nat.add_right_cancel htemp2`.
5. Now apply `List.append_inj` to `h_eq_cat` and `hylen_eq_ulen.symm`? Wait: `List.append_inj` expects `a ++ b = c ++ d` and `length a = length c`. Here we have `u ++ x = y ++ v`. The length equality we need is `u.length = y.length`. We have `hylen_eq_ulen` gives `y.length = u.length`, so `u.length = y.length` is `hylen_eq_ulen.symm`. So we can do:
   `have hsplit := List.append_inj h_eq_cat hylen_eq_ulen.symm`
   This gives `hsplit.1 : u = y` and `hsplit.2 : x = v`.
6. Now rewrite `w` using `hwx` and then `hsplit.2`:
   `rw [hwx, hsplit.2, ← Word.mul_eq_concat]`? Actually `⬝` is `Word.concat` which is `List.append`. So `u ⬝ v` is `u ++ v`. So `rw [hwx, hsplit.2]` yields `u ++ v`, which is `u ⬝ v` by `rfl`. So we can just `rw [hwx, hsplit.2]`.
7. The proof is complete.

--- Planning Phase (Iteration 3/3) ---

[PlannerAgent] Reasoning:
The previous plans attempted to use `IsPrefix.def` and `IsSuffix.def`, but the definitions of `IsPrefix` and `IsSuffix` are directly `List.IsPrefix` and `List.IsSuffix`, which are defined as `∃ t, w = u ++ t` and `∃ t, w = t ++ u` respectively. This means we can directly `obtain` witnesses from the hypotheses without unfolding `def`. The proof then follows by equating the two decompositions, using the length condition to obtain equalities of the witness lengths via `Nat.add_right_cancel`, and applying `List.append_inj` to conclude equality of the components, ultimately giving `w = u ⬝ v`.

[PlannerAgent] Plan:

3. Derive `h_cat : u ++ x = y ++ v` by `rw [← hx, hy]`.
4. Compute the length of `w` from the first decomposition:
   `have hw_len_x : w.length = u.length + x.length := by simpa [List.length_append] using congrArg Word.length hx`
   (We note that `Word.length` is `List.length`, so `simpa` with `List.length_append` works.)

   `have h_sum_xv : u.length + x.length = u.length + v.length := by linarith`
   (We can use `linarith` if `linarith` is imported; else use `calc` with `rw`.)
   We'll use `calc` with rewriting to avoid `linarith` dependency, but `linarith` works with natural numbers? `linarith` does work with `Nat` but `omega` is better. Simpler: use `rw` and `exact`:
   `have h_sum_xv : u.length + x.length = u.length + v.length := by rw [← hw_len_x, hlen]`
6. Cancel `u.length` from both sides using `Nat.add_right_cancel` to get `hx_len : x.length = v.length`:
   `have hx_len : x.length = v.length := Nat.add_right_cancel h_sum_xv`
7. Similarly, from `hy`, compute `hw_len_y : w.length = y.length + v.length` (by `simpa [List.length_append] using congrArg Word.length hy`).
   Then `h_sum_yu : y.length + v.length = u.length + v.length := by rw [← hw_len_y, hlen]`
   Cancel `v.length` with `Nat.add_right_cancel` to get `hy_len' : y.length = u.length`.
   Then `hy_len : u.length = y.length := hy_len'.symm`.
8. Apply `List.append_inj` to `h_cat` and `hy_len` to obtain a pair `⟨hu_eq_y, hx_eq_v⟩` where `hu_eq_y : u = y` and `hx_eq_v : x = v`.
9. Rewrite `hx` using `hx_eq_v`: `rw [hx, hx_eq_v]` to get `w = u ++ v`.
10. Finally, `simpa [Word.concat]` because `⬝` is defined as `++`.

[PlannerAgent] Reasoning:
The goal is to show that if `u` is a prefix of `v` and `v` is a proper prefix of `w`, then `u` is a proper prefix of `w`. The definition of `IsProperPrefix u w` is `u ≤ₚ w ∧ u ≠ w`. So we need both conjuncts. We obtain `u ≤ₚ w` by transitivity of `IsPrefix` (lemma `IsPrefix.trans`). The inequality `u ≠ w` can be shown using length comparison: from `hvw : v <ₚ w` we have `v.length < w.length` (lemma `IsProperPrefix.length_lt`), and from `huv : u ≤ₚ v` we have `u.length ≤ v.length` (lemma `IsPrefix.length_le`). Combining, `u.length < w.length`, so `u ≠ w`. No additional lemmas are needed; all are in the CoW library.

   - From `IsProperPrefix.length_lt hvw` we get `h_vw_len : v.length < w.length`.

[PlannerAgent] Reasoning:
To avoid subtle length arithmetic and keep the proof structural, we use the definitional characterization of proper prefix: `IsProperPrefix u w` holds iff there exists a non‑empty suffix `t` such that `w = u ⬝ t`. From `huv : u <ₚ v` we obtain such a suffix `x` for `v`, and from `hvw : v ≤ₚ w` we obtain a suffix `y` such that `w = v ⬝ y`. Composing, `w = u ⬝ (x ⬝ y)` with `x ⬝ y` non‑empty because `x` is. This directly yields the proper prefix relation. All needed lemmas are in the CoW context.

[PlannerAgent] Plan:

2. Use `(IsPrefix.def v w).mp hvw` to obtain `y` and `hy : w = v ++ y`.
3. Combine to express `w`:
   - `rw [hx]` at `hy` to get `hy' : w = (u ++ x) ++ y`.
   - Apply `List.append_assoc` to rewrite `(u ++ x) ++ y` as `u ++ (x ++ y)`.
   So we have `hw : w = u ++ (x ++ y)`.
4. Show that the suffix `(x ++ y)` is non‑empty:
   - Assume `h_empty : x ++ y = []`.
   - By `List.append_eq_nil.mp h_empty`, deduce `hx_nil : x = []`, which contradicts `hx_ne`.
   - Hence `h_tail_ne : x ++ y ≠ []`.
5. Apply `(IsProperPrefix.def u w).mpr` with witness `(x ++ y)`:
   - Provide `⟨x ++ y, by simpa [Word.concat, hw] using rfl, h_tail_ne⟩`.
   (Alternatively `⟨x ++ y, by
       rw [Word.concat, ← hw, Word.concat]; rfl, h_tail_ne⟩`)
6. This completes the proof.

   - This contradicts `Nat.ne_of_lt h_len_lt`. So `h_ne : u ≠ w := λ heq => (Nat.ne_of_lt h_len_lt) (congrArg Word.length heq)`.
4. Return `⟨h_pre, h_ne⟩`.

   - `hx_nil` contradicts `hx_ne`.

We can prove each direction separately with simple intro/apply/contradiction patterns. No external lemmas beyond basic logic are required.

[PlannerAgent] Plan:

   - Assume `h_unb : IsUnbordered w`.
   - From `h_ex`, obtain `b`, `h_bord`, `h_ne`.
   - Apply `h_unb` to `b` and `h_bord` to get `b = []`, which contradicts `h_ne`.
2. **Reverse direction** (`¬ IsUnbordered w → ∃ b, IsBorder b w ∧ b ≠ []`):
   - Assume `h_not_unb : ¬ IsUnbordered w`.
   - Show `∃ b, IsBorder b w ∧ b ≠ []` by contradiction: assume `h_no_border : ¬ ∃ b, IsBorder b w ∧ b ≠ []`.
   - Show that `IsUnbordered w` holds: take any `b` and `h_bord : IsBorder b w`. If `b ≠ []`, then we would have `∃ b, IsBorder b w ∧ b ≠ []` (by providing `b`), contradicting `h_no_border`. Hence `b = []`.
   - Thus `IsUnbordered w` is proved, which contradicts `h_not_unb`.
   - Therefore the contradiction yields the desired existential.
3. The proof uses only the definitions of `IsUnbordered`, `IsBorder`, and basic quantifier reasoning.

[Orchestrator] Initiating Multi-Agent Repair for border_nonempty_implies_length_ge_two
[Orchestrator] Loaded CoW source context (26169 chars).

==================================================
--- Planning Phase (Iteration 1/3) ---

[PlannerAgent] Reasoning:
Given `hb : IsBorder b w` and `hne : b ≠ []`, we need to show `2 ≤ w.length`. Since `b` is a border, it is a proper prefix, so `b.length < w.length` (by `IsBorder.length_lt`). Also `b ≠ []` implies `0 < b.length` (via `List.length_pos_iff_ne_nil`). From `0 < b.length` we get `1 ≤ b.length`. Then `b.length + 1 ≤ w.length` because `b.length < w.length` implies `Nat.succ_le_of_lt`. Finally, `2 ≤ b.length + 1` because `1 ≤ b.length`. Transitivity yields `2 ≤ w.length`. All needed lemmas are in the CoW context and Mathlib.

[PlannerAgent] Plan:
1. From `hb : IsBorder b w` obtain `h_len_lt : b.length < w.length` using `IsBorder.length_lt hb`.
2. From `hne : b ≠ []` obtain `hpos : 0 < b.length` using `List.length_pos_iff_ne_nil.mpr hne`.
3. From `hpos` deduce `h_ge_one : 1 ≤ b.length` via `Nat.succ_le_of_lt hpos`.
4. From `h_len_lt` deduce `h_succ_le : b.length + 1 ≤ w.length` via `Nat.succ_le_of_lt h_len_lt`.
5. Combine to get `2 ≤ w.length`:
   ```
   have h_two_le : 2 ≤ w.length := by
     calc
       2 = 1 + 1 := by norm_num
       _ ≤ b.length + 1 := Nat.add_le_add_right h_ge_one 1
       _ ≤ w.length := h_succ_le
   exact h_two_le
   ```
   (Alternatively, `omega` can handle the arithmetic; the explicit `calc` is safe.)
6. The proof is complete.

[Orchestrator] Loaded CoW source context (26169 chars).

--- Planning Phase (Iteration 1/3) ---

[PlannerAgent] Reasoning:
The theorem states that a border `b` of a word `w` induces a period of length `w.length - b.length`. This is a classic result: if `b` is both a proper prefix and a proper suffix, then the word is periodic with period equal to the length of the suffix/prefix complement. The proof uses the decompositions `w = b ++ x` and `w = y ++ b` (with `x`, `y` non‑empty), deduces `|x| = |y| = w.length - b.length`, and then checks the periodicity condition by comparing `w[i]` and `w[i + |x|]` for indices where `i + |x|` is still within the word. The length inequality reduces to `i < |b|`, and the equality follows directly from the decompositions using `List.get?_append_left` and `List.get?_append_right`. All required lemmas are in the CoW library and Mathlib.

[PlannerAgent] Plan:
1. From `h : IsBorder b w`, obtain `hb_pre : b <ₚ w` and `hb_suf : b <ₛ w` (via `h.1` and `h.2`).
2. Apply `(IsProperPrefix.def b w).mp hb_pre` to get `x` with `(hw_pre : w = b ++ x)` and `(hx_ne : x ≠ [])`.
3. Apply `(IsProperSuffix.iff b w).mp hb_suf` to get `y` with `(hw_suf : w = y ++ b)` and `(hy_ne : y ≠ [])`.
4. Use `List.length_append` on each decomposition to obtain:
   - `hlen_pre : w.length = b.length + x.length`.
   - `hlen_suf : w.length = y.length + b.length`.
   From these derive `h_len_eq : x.length = y.length` by subtracting `b.length` from both sides (using `omega` or `Nat.add_right_cancel` on `hlen_pre.trans hlen_suf.symm` after moving terms).
5. Set `p := w.length - b.length`. Show `hp_pos : 0 < p` using `h_blt : b.length < w.length` (from `IsBorder.length_lt h`) and `Nat.sub_pos_of_lt h_blt`.
6. Show that `p = x.length` using `hlen_pre` and `Nat.add_sub_cancel_left`:
   `calc w.length - b.length = (b.length + x.length) - b.length := by rw [hlen_pre] ... = x.length := by simpa using Nat.add_sub_cancel_left (b.length) (x.length)`. 	Thus `h_p_eq : p = x.length`.
7. To prove `HasPeriod w p` we need `0 < p` (already done) and the main condition.
   For any `i` with `h_bound : i + p < w.length`, we need `w.get? i = w.get? (i + p)`.
   - From `h_bound` and `hlen_pre` we get `i + p < b.length + x.length`. Using `h_p_eq : p = x.length`, rewrite to `i + x.length < b.length + x.length`. Cancel `x.length` to obtain `hi_lt_b : i < b.length`.
   - Now compute `w.get? i` via `hw_pre`:
     `w.get? i = (b ++ x).get? i = b.get? i` (by `List.get?_append_left hi_lt_b`).
   - Compute `w.get? (i + p)` via `hw_suf`: `w = y ++ b`. Using `h_len_eq : x.length = y.length` and `h_p_eq` we know `p = y.length`. Thus `i + p = i + y.length`.
     Since `y.length ≤ i + y.length` (trivial), apply `List.get?_append_right` (with condition `y.length ≤ i + y.length`; `exact Nat.le_add_left _ _`) to obtain
     `(y ++ b).get? (i + y.length) = b.get? ((i + y.length) - y.length)`.
   - Simplify `(i + y.length) - y.length = i` using `Nat.add_sub_cancel_right`.
     Hence `w.get? (i + p) = b.get? i`.
   - Conclude equality.
8. Assemble everything into `HasPeriod w p`.

```lean4
have h_blt : b.length < w.length := IsBorder.length_lt h
  have hp_pos : 0 < w.length - b.length := Nat.sub_pos_of_lt h_blt
  obtain ⟨x, hw_pre, hx_ne⟩ := (IsProperPrefix.def b w).mp h.1
  obtain ⟨y, hw_suf, hy_ne⟩ := (IsProperSuffix.iff b w).mp h.2
  have hlen_pre : w.length = b.length + x.length := by
    rw [hw_pre, Word.length_concat]
  have hlen_suf : w.length = y.length + b.length := by
    rw [hw_suf, Word.length_concat]
  have h_len_eq : x.length = y.length := by
    have h_eq : b.length + x.length = y.length + b.length := by
      rw [← hlen_pre, hlen_suf]
    have h_eq' : b.length + x.length = b.length + y.length := by

    rw [List.get?_append_right h_le]

  rw [hleft, hright]
```

--- Planning Phase (Iteration 2/3) ---

[PlannerAgent] Reasoning:
Given `b` is a border of `w`, we have `b <ₚ w` and `b <ₛ w`. From these we get decompositions `w = b ++ x` with `x ≠ []` and `w = y ++ b` with `y ≠ []`. The lengths give `w.length - b.length = x.length = y.length`. To show `HasPeriod w p` where `p = w.length - b.length`, we need `0 < p` (which follows from `b.length < w.length`, a property of a border) and for every `i` with `i + p < w.length`, the characters at positions `i` and `i + p` coincide. By writing `i + p = i + x.length` and using the two decompositions, the prefix part gives `w[i] = b[i]` when `i < b.length`, while the suffix part gives `w[i + x.length] = (y ++ b)[i + y.length] = b[i]`. Hence equality.

All used lemmas (`IsBorder.length_lt`, `IsProperPrefix.def`, `IsProperSuffix.iff`, `Word.length_concat`, `Nat.sub_pos_of_lt`, `Nat.add_sub_cancel_left`, `Nat.add_sub_cancel_right`, `Nat.add_lt_add_right`, `List.get?_append_left`, `List.get?_append_right`, `Nat.le_add_left`, `Nat.add_sub_cancel_right`) are available in the imported CoW and Mathlib libraries.

[PlannerAgent] Plan:
1. From `h : IsBorder b w`, derive `h_blt : b.length < w.length` using `IsBorder.length_lt h`.
2. Show `hp_pos : 0 < w.length - b.length` using `Nat.sub_pos_of_lt h_blt`.
3. Obtain the prefix decomposition: `rcases (IsProperPrefix.def b w).mp h.1` to get `x`, `hw_pre : w = b ++ x`, and `hx_ne : x ≠ []`.
4. Obtain the suffix decomposition: `rcases (IsProperSuffix.iff b w).mp h.2` to get `y`, `hw_suf : w = y ++ b`, and `hy_ne : y ≠ []`.
5. Compute `hlen_pre : w.length = b.length + x.length` by `rw [hw_pre, Word.length_concat]`.
   Compute `hlen_suf : w.length = y.length + b.length` by `rw [hw_suf, Word.length_concat]`.
6. Get `hpx : w.length - b.length = x.length` from `hlen_pre` and `Nat.add_sub_cancel_left`.
   Get `hpy : w.length - b.length = y.length` from `hlen_suf` and `Nat.add_sub_cancel_right`.
   Then `h_len_eq : x.length = y.length` follows by `calc` or `rw`.
7. Assemble the `HasPeriod` witness:
   - `refine ⟨hp_pos, λ i hi_bound => ?_⟩`.
   - In the inner proof, rewrite the period using `hpx` and `hpy` at convenience.
   - Prove `hi_lt_b : i < b.length` by:
       * `rw [hpx]` at `hi_bound` gives `i + x.length < w.length`.
       * `rw [hlen_pre]` at this to get `i + x.length < b.length + x.length`.
       * Apply `Nat.add_lt_add_right` or `Nat.lt_of_add_lt_add_right` to obtain `hi_lt_b`.

   - Conclude equality.

[PlannerAgent] Reasoning:
The duality follows by decomposing `w` as a prefix `b ++ x` and as a suffix `y ++ b`, using the fact that `|x| = |y| = w.length - b.length`. The periodicity condition reduces to showing that for any index `i` with `i + (w.length - b.length) < w.length`, we have `w[i] = w[i + (w.length - b.length)]`. By the length arithmetic, such `i` must be smaller than `|b|`, so the left character is `b[i]`. Using the suffix decomposition, the character at `i + |y|` is also `b[i]`. The proof uses only `List.length_append`, `List.get?_append`, and basic `Nat` cancellation lemmas already available in `Mathlib.Data.List.Basic` and `Mathlib.Data.Nat.Basic`.

<plan>
1. From `h : IsBorder b w`, obtain `h_blt : b.length < w.length` via `IsBorder.length_lt h`.
2. Set `p := w.length - b.length`. Prove `hp_pos : 0 < p` using `Nat.sub_pos_of_lt h_blt`.
3. Use `(IsProperPrefix.def b w).mp h.1` to get `x` with `hw_pre : w = b ++ x` and `hx_ne : x ≠ []`.
4. Use `(IsProperSuffix.iff b w).mp h.2` to get `y` with `hw_suf : w = y ++ b` and `hy_ne : y ≠ []`.
5. Compute lengths:
   - `hlen_pre : w.length = b.length + x.length` via `rw [hw_pre, Word.length_concat]`.
   - `hlen_suf : w.length = y.length + b.length` via `rw [hw_suf, Word.length_concat]`.
6. Show `h_len_eq : x.length = y.length`:
   - `have h_eq : b.length + x.length = b.length + y.length := by
        rw [← hlen_pre, hlen_suf, add_comm y.length b.length]`
   - `exact Nat.add_right_cancel h_eq`.
7. Show `h_p_eq : p = x.length` via `rw [hlen_pre, Nat.add_sub_cancel_left]`.
8. For `HasPeriod w p`, return `⟨hp_pos, λ i hi_bound => ?_⟩`.
   - `hi_bound : i + p < w.length`.
   - Using `h_p_eq` and `hlen_pre`, rewrite `hi_bound` as `i + x.length < b.length + x.length`.
   - Deduce `hi_lt_b : i < b.length` by `apply Nat.lt_of_add_lt_add_right; simpa [h_p_eq, hlen_pre] using hi_bound`.
   - Left side equality:
     `rw [hw_pre]` to get `(b ++ x).get? i`.
     `simpa [List.get?_append, hi_lt_b]` to obtain `b.get? i`.
   - Right side equality:
     `rw [hw_suf, h_p_eq, h_len_eq]`. Now the goal is `(y ++ b).get? (i + y.length) = b.get? i`.
     `simpa [List.get?_append, Nat.add_sub_cancel_right]` because `i + y.length ≮ y.length`.
   - Combine by rewriting both sides to `b.get? i`.
</plan>

```lean4
by
  have h_blt : b.length < w.length := IsBorder.length_lt h
  set p := w.length - b.length with hp_def
  have hp_pos : 0 < p := Nat.sub_pos_of_lt h_blt
  obtain ⟨x, hw_pre, hx_ne⟩ := (IsProperPrefix.def b w).mp h.1
  obtain ⟨y, hw_suf, hy_ne⟩ := (IsProperSuffix.iff b w).mp h.2
  have hlen_pre : w.length = b.length + x.length := by
    rw [hw_pre, Word.length_concat]
  have hlen_suf : w.length = y.length + b.length := by
    rw [hw_suf, Word.length_concat]
  have h_len_eq : x.length = y.length := by
    have h_eq : b.length + x.length = b.length + y.length := by
      rw [← hlen_pre, hlen_suf, add_comm y.length b.length]
    exact Nat.add_right_cancel h_eq
  have h_p_eq : p = x.length := by
    rw [hp_def, hlen_pre, Nat.add_sub_cancel_left]
  have hi_bound_condition (i : ℕ) (hi_bound : i + p < w.length) : i < b.length := by
    have htemp : i + x.length < b.length + x.length := by
      rw [← h_p_eq, ← hlen_pre]
      exact hi_bound
    exact Nat.lt_of_add_lt_add_right htemp
  refine ⟨hp_pos, λ i hi_bound => ?_⟩
  have hi_lt_b : i < b.length := hi_bound_condition i hi_bound
  have hleft : w.get? i = b.get? i := by
    rw [hw_pre, List.get?_append_left hi_lt_b]
  have hright : w.get? (i + p) = b.get? i := by
    rw [h_p_eq, h_len_eq, hw_suf, List.get?_append_right (Nat.le_add_right y.length i),
      Nat.add_sub_cancel_right]
  rw [hleft, hright]
```

--- Planning Phase (Iteration 1/3) ---

[PlannerAgent] Reasoning:
The statement follows directly from the definition of `IsUnbordered w`, which is `∀ b, IsBorder b w → b = []`. Given a non‑empty border `b`, assuming `IsUnbordered w` would force `b = []`, contradicting the hypothesis `hne : b ≠ []`. Thus `¬ IsUnbordered w`. No additional lemmas are needed.

[PlannerAgent] Plan:
1. Assume `h : IsBorder b w` and `hne : b ≠ []`.
2. Introduce `hunb : IsUnbordered w`.
3. Apply `hunb` to `b` and `h` to get `hb_eq : b = []`.
4. Combine `hne` and `hb_eq` to obtain a contradiction.
5. Conclude `¬ IsUnbordered w`.
The proof is a one-liner:
```lean4
theorem border_imp_not_unbordered {b w : Word α} (h : IsBorder b w) (hne : b ≠ []) : ¬ IsUnbordered w :=
  λ hunb => hne (hunb b h)
```

[Orchestrator] Loaded CoW source context (26169 chars).

==================================================
--- Planning Phase (Iteration 1/3) ---

[PlannerAgent] Reasoning:
The theorem is a direct consequence of the definition of conjugacy and the basic property that concatenation is empty only if both components are empty. From `h : u ~ []`, we obtain `x` and `y` with `u = x ⬝ y` and `[] = y ⬝ x`. The second equation yields `y ++ x = []`, which by `List.append_eq_nil` forces `y = []` and `x = []`. Substituting back into the first equation gives `u = []`. All required lemmas (`List.append_eq_nil`) are in the imported `Data.List.Basic`.

[PlannerAgent] Plan:
1. Unfold the definition of `IsConjugate` in `h` to obtain `x`, `y`, `hu : u = x ⬝ y`, and `hnil : [] = y ⬝ x`.
2. Rewrite `hnil` symmetrically: `have hnil' : y ++ x = [] := by simpa [Word.concat] using hnil.symm`. (Or simply `have hnil' := hnil.symm` because `⬝` is definitionally `++`.)
3. Apply `List.append_eq_nil.mp` to `hnil'` to get `⟨hy_nil : y = [], hx_nil : x = []⟩`.
4. Substitute `hx_nil` and `hy_nil` into `hu`: `rw [hx_nil, hy_nil] at hu`.
5. Simplify `hu` (which becomes `u = [] ⬝ []`) to `u = []` using `simp`.
6. `exact hu`.

[31/45]      Conjugacy | MEDIUM | conjugate_concat_rotate

[Orchestrator] Loaded CoW source context (26169 chars).

==================================================
--- Planning Phase (Iteration 1/3) ---

[PlannerAgent] Reasoning:
The goal `(u ⬝ v ⬝ w) ~ (v ⬝ w ⬝ u)` follows directly from the definition of conjugacy by choosing `x := u` and `y := v ⬝ w`. Then we need `(u ⬝ v ⬝ w) = u ⬝ (v ⬝ w)` and `(v ⬝ w ⬝ u) = (v ⬝ w) ⬝ u`, both of which hold by associativity of concatenation (`Word.concat_assoc` or `List.append_assoc`). All required lemmas are available.

[PlannerAgent] Plan:
1. Use `refine ⟨u, v ⬝ w, ?_, ?_⟩`.
2. First goal: `u ⬝ v ⬝ w = u ⬝ (v ⬝ w)`. This is true by associativity: `(u ⬝ v) ⬝ w = u ⬝ (v ⬝ w)`. Actually `u ⬝ v ⬝ w` is left-assoc: `(u ⬝ v) ⬝ w`. So we need `(u ⬝ v) ⬝ w = u ⬝ (v ⬝ w)`, which is `Word.concat_assoc u v w`. So `rw [Word.concat_assoc]`.
3. Second goal: `v ⬝ w ⬝ u = (v ⬝ w) ⬝ u`. This is also `(v ⬝ w) ⬝ u = (v ⬝ w) ⬝ u`, trivial `rfl`. But note the left side is `(v ⬝ w) ⬝ u` by association, so `rfl` works. Alternatively `simpa [Word.concat_assoc]`.
4. The proof: `refine ⟨u, v ⬝ w, by rw [Word.concat_assoc], rfl⟩`.

--- Planning Phase (Iteration 2/3) ---

[PlannerAgent] Reasoning:
The proof can be done structurally using the explicit decomposition of conjugacy. From `h : u ~ v`, we obtain `x, y` such that `u = x ⬝ y` and `v = y ⬝ x`. If `v = []`, then `y ⬝ x = []`. Since `⬝` is `List.append`, we apply `List.append_eq_nil` to deduce `y = []` and `x = []`. Substituting back into the expression for `u` gives `u = []`, contradicting `hu`. This avoids length arithmetic entirely and uses only `List.append_eq_nil`, which is already in the imports.

[PlannerAgent] Plan:
1. Use `rcases h with ⟨x, y, hu_eq, hv_eq⟩`.
2. Assume `hv_nil : v = []`. Then `rw [hv_nil]` at `hv_eq` (or `rw` to see `v = y ⬝ x` becomes `[] = y ⬝ x`). So we have `h_empty : y ⬝ x = []` (or `y ++ x = []`).
3. Apply `List.append_eq_nil.mp` to `h_empty` to obtain `hy : y = []` and `hx : x = []`.
4. Substitute `hx` and `hy` into `hu_eq` to get `u = [] ⬝ []`, which simplifies to `u = []`.
5. This contradicts `hu`. Hence `v ≠ []`.

[PlannerAgent] Reasoning:
The proof follows directly from the structural decomposition of conjugacy and the fact that concatenation of words is non‑empty if any component is non‑empty. Using `List.append_eq_nil` we can deduce that if the conjugated word is empty, then its constituent parts are empty, forcing the original word to be empty, contradicting the hypothesis `hu`. The plan avoids length arithmetic entirely.

<plan>

   `have ⟨hy_nil, hx_nil⟩ := List.append_eq_nil.mp h_empty`

   `rw [hx_nil, hy_nil] at hu_eq`
6. Simplify `hu_eq` (which becomes `u = [] ⬝ []`) to `u = []` using `simp` (or `simpa` using `hu_eq`).
7. The resulting equation `u = []` contradicts the hypothesis `hu : u ≠ []`. Conclude `v ≠ []`.
</plan>

[34/45]      Conjugacy |   HARD | conjugate_pow_of_conjugate

[Orchestrator] Initiating Multi-Agent Repair for conjugate_pow_of_conjugate
[Orchestrator] Loaded CoW source context (26169 chars).

==================================================
--- Planning Phase (Iteration 1/3) ---

[PlannerAgent] Reasoning:
The theorem follows directly from the definition of conjugacy and the identity `(x ⬝ y)^(n+1) = x ⬝ ((y ⬝ x)^n) ⬝ y`. Given `h : u ~ v`, we obtain `x`, `y` such that `u = x ⬝ y` and `v = y ⬝ x`. For any `n`, if `n = 0` the result is trivial. For `n = m+1`, we can exhibit `a := x` and `b := (v^m) ⬝ y` as conjugacy witnesses. The required equalities are `u^(m+1) = a ⬝ b` (which follows from the identity above) and `v^(m+1) = b ⬝ a` (which follows from associativity and the definition of `v`). The auxiliary identity is proved by induction on `m` using only `Word.pow_succ` and `Word.concat_assoc`. All required lemmas are in the CoW context.

[PlannerAgent] Plan:
1. `rcases h with ⟨x, y, hu, hv⟩`.
2. Prove the auxiliary lemma `hstep (a : Word α) : (x ⬝ a ⬝ y) ⬝ (x ⬝ y) = x ⬝ (a ⬝ (y ⬝ x)) ⬝ y` using `Word.concat_assoc`.
3. Use `hstep` to prove by induction `h_id : ∀ n, (x ⬝ y) ^ (n+1) = x ⬝ ((y ⬝ x) ^ n) ⬝ y`.
   - Base case `n=0`: `simp`.
   - Inductive step: `calc` with `Word.pow_succ`, induction hypothesis, `hstep`, and `Word.pow_succ`.
4. Now consider the goal `u ^ n ~ v ^ n`.
   - If `n = 0`, `simp` or `IsConjugate.refl`.
   - If `n = m+1`, provide conjugacy witnesses:
     * `a := x`
     * `b := ((y ⬝ x) ^ m) ⬝ y`
   - Show `u ^ (m+1) = a ⬝ b`:
     `calc u ^ (m+1) = (x ⬝ y) ^ (m+1) := by rw [hu] ... = x ⬝ (((y ⬝ x) ^ m) ⬝ y) := by rw [h_id m, Word.concat_assoc]; ... = a ⬝ b := rfl`.
   - Show `v ^ (m+1) = b ⬝ a`:
     `calc v ^ (m+1) = v ^ m ⬝ v := Word.pow_succ v m ... = ((y ⬝ x) ^ m) ⬝ (y ⬝ x) := by rw [hv] ... = (((y ⬝ x) ^ m) ⬝ y) ⬝ x := by rw [Word.concat_assoc] ... = b ⬝ a := rfl`.
   - Conclude with `⟨a, b, ...⟩`.
5. This completes the proof.


--- Builder Execution (Attempt 1/3) ---
[Orchestrator] ⚠️  Proof contains 'sorry' — treating as incomplete.
[Orchestrator] Applying Patch...
```lean4
rcases h with ⟨x, y, hu, hv⟩
  have hstep (a : Word α) : (x ⬝ a ⬝ y) ⬝ (x ⬝ y) = x ⬝ (a ⬝ (y ⬝ x)) ⬝ y := by
    calc
      (x ⬝ a ⬝ y) ⬝ (x ⬝ y) = ((x ⬝ a) ⬝ y) ⬝ (x ⬝ y) := rfl
      _ = (x ⬝ a) ⬝ (y ⬝ (x ⬝ y)) := by rw [Word.concat_assoc]
      _ = (x ⬝ a) ⬝ ((y ⬝ x) ⬝ y) := by rw [Word.concat_assoc]
      _ = x ⬝ (a ⬝ ((y ⬝ x) ⬝ y)) := by rw [Word.concat_assoc]
      _ = x ⬝ ((a ⬝ (y ⬝ x)) ⬝ y) := by rw [Word.concat_assoc]
      _ = x ⬝ (a ⬝ (y ⬝ x)) ⬝ y := rfl
  have h_id : ∀ n : ℕ, (x ⬝ y) ^ (n + 1) = x ⬝ ((y ⬝ x) ^ n) ⬝ y := by
    intro n
    induction n with
    | zero => simp
    | succ m ih =>
        calc
          (x ⬝ y) ^ ((m + 1) + 1) = (x ⬝ y) ^ (m + 1) ⬝ (x ⬝ y) := by rw [Word.pow_succ]
          _ = (x ⬝ ((y ⬝ x) ^ m) ⬝ y) ⬝ (x ⬝ y) := by rw [ih]
          _ = x ⬝ (((y ⬝ x) ^ m) ⬝ (y ⬝ x)) ⬝ y := by rw [hstep]
          _ = x ⬝ ((y ⬝ x) ^ (m + 1)) ⬝ y := by rw [Word.pow_succ]
  cases n with
  | zero =>
      exact IsConjugate.refl _
  | succ m =>
      set a := x with ha
      set b := ((y ⬝ x) ^ m) ⬝ y with hb
      have h_eq1 : u ^ (m + 1) = a ⬝ b := by
        rw [hu, h_id m, ha, hb]
        rw [Word.concat_assoc]
      have h_eq2 : v ^ (m + 1) = b ⬝ a := by
        calc
          v ^ (m + 1) = v ^ m ⬝ v := by rw [Word.pow_succ]
          _ = ((y ⬝ x) ^ m) ⬝ (y ⬝ x) := by rw [hv]
          _ = ((y ⬝ x) ^ m) ⬝ y ⬝ x := by rw [Word.concat_assoc]
          _ = b ⬝ a := rfl
      exact ⟨a, b, h_eq1, h_eq2⟩
```

--- Builder Execution (Attempt 2/3) ---
[Orchestrator] Applying Patch...
```lean4
by
  rcases h with ⟨x, y, hu, hv⟩
  have h_id : ∀ n : ℕ, (x ⬝ y) ^ (n + 1) = x ⬝ ((y ⬝ x) ^ n) ⬝ y := by
    intro n
    induction n with
    | zero => simp
    | succ m ih =>

          (x ⬝ y) ^ ((m + 1) + 1) = (x ⬝ y) ^ (m + 1) ⬝ (x ⬝ y) := by rw [Word.pow_succ]
          _ = (x ⬝ ((y ⬝ x) ^ m) ⬝ y) ⬝ (x ⬝ y) := by rw [ih]
          _ = x ⬝ (((y ⬝ x) ^ m) ⬝ (y ⬝ x)) ⬝ y := by
            calc
              (x ⬝ ((y ⬝ x) ^ m) ⬝ y) ⬝ (x ⬝ y) = ((x ⬝ ((y ⬝ x) ^ m)) ⬝ y) ⬝ (x ⬝ y) := rfl
              _ = (x ⬝ ((y ⬝ x) ^ m)) ⬝ (y ⬝ (x ⬝ y)) := by rw [Word.concat_assoc]
              _ = (x ⬝ ((y ⬝ x) ^ m)) ⬝ ((y ⬝ x) ⬝ y) := by rw [Word.concat_assoc]
              _ = x ⬝ (((y ⬝ x) ^ m) ⬝ ((y ⬝ x) ⬝ y)) := by rw [Word.concat_assoc]
              _ = x ⬝ ((((y ⬝ x) ^ m) ⬝ (y ⬝ x)) ⬝ y) := by rw [Word.concat_assoc]
              _ = x ⬝ (((y ⬝ x) ^ m) ⬝ (y ⬝ x)) ⬝ y := by rw [Word.concat_assoc]
          _ = x ⬝ ((y ⬝ x) ^ (m + 1)) ⬝ y := by rw [Word.pow_succ]
  cases n with
  | zero => simpa using IsConjugate.refl (1 : Word α)
  | succ m =>
      refine ⟨x, ((y ⬝ x) ^ m) ⬝ y, ?_, ?_⟩
      · calc
          u ^ (m + 1) = (x ⬝ y) ^ (m + 1) := by rw [hu]
          _ = x ⬝ ((y ⬝ x) ^ m) ⬝ y := by rw [h_id m]
          _ = x ⬝ (((y ⬝ x) ^ m) ⬝ y) := by rw [Word.concat_assoc]
      · calc
          v ^ (m + 1) = v ^ m ⬝ v := by rw [Word.pow_succ]
          _ = ((y ⬝ x) ^ m) ⬝ (y ⬝ x) := by rw [hv]
          _ = ((y ⬝ x) ^ m) ⬝ y ⬝ x := by rw [Word.concat_assoc]
```

```lean4
rcases h with ⟨x, y, hu, hv⟩
have h_comm : ∀ n : ℕ, (x ⬝ y) ^ n ⬝ x = x ⬝ (y ⬝ x) ^ n := by
  intro n
  induction n with
  | zero => simp
  | succ m ih =>
    calc
      (x ⬝ y) ^ (m + 1) ⬝ x = ((x ⬝ y) ^ m ⬝ (x ⬝ y)) ⬝ x := by rw [Word.pow_succ]
      _ = (x ⬝ y) ^ m ⬝ ((x ⬝ y) ⬝ x) := by rw [Word.concat_assoc]
      _ = (x ⬝ y) ^ m ⬝ (x ⬝ (y ⬝ x)) := by rw [Word.concat_assoc]
      _ = ((x ⬝ y) ^ m ⬝ x) ⬝ (y ⬝ x) := by rw [← Word.concat_assoc]
      _ = (x ⬝ (y ⬝ x) ^ m) ⬝ (y ⬝ x) := by rw [ih]
      _ = x ⬝ ((y ⬝ x) ^ m ⬝ (y ⬝ x)) := by rw [Word.concat_assoc]
      _ = x ⬝ (y ⬝ x) ^ (m + 1) := by rw [Word.pow_succ]
have h_id : ∀ n : ℕ, (x ⬝ y) ^ (n + 1) = x ⬝ ((y ⬝ x) ^ n) ⬝ y := by
  intro n
  calc
    (x ⬝ y) ^ (n + 1) = (x ⬝ y) ^ n ⬝ (x ⬝ y) := by rw [Word.pow_succ]
    _ = ((x ⬝ y) ^ n ⬝ x) ⬝ y := by rw [← Word.concat_assoc]
    _ = (x ⬝ (y ⬝ x) ^ n) ⬝ y := by rw [h_comm n]
    _ = x ⬝ ((y ⬝ x) ^ n) ⬝ y := rfl
cases n with
| zero =>
    simpa [Word.pow_zero] using IsConjugate.refl ([] : Word α)
| succ m =>

        _ = x ⬝ (((y ⬝ x) ^ m) ⬝ y) := by rw [Word.concat_assoc]
```

[Orchestrator] Initiating Multi-Agent Repair for pow_two_not_primitive
[Orchestrator] Loaded CoW source context (26169 chars).

==================================================
--- Planning Phase (Iteration 1/3) ---

[PlannerAgent] Reasoning:
The definition of `IsPrimitive w` is `w ≠ [] ∧ ¬ ∃ (u : Word α) (k : ℕ), k ≥ 2 ∧ w = u ^ k`. Thus `¬ IsPrimitive (w ⬝ w)` is equivalent to `(w ⬝ w = []) ∨ (∃ u k, k ≥ 2 ∧ w ⬝ w = u ^ k)`. Since `w ≠ []`, the left disjunct is impossible (otherwise `List.append_eq_nil` would force `w = []`). So we provide the right disjunct by choosing `u := w` and `k := 2`. The equality `w ⬝ w = w ^ 2` follows from `Word.pow_succ w 1` and `Word.pow_one w`:
`w ^ 2 = w ^ (1+1) = w ^ 1 ⬝ w = w ⬝ w`.
All lemmas are in the context.

[PlannerAgent] Plan:
1. Assume `hprim : IsPrimitive (w ⬝ w)` with the goal of deriving `False`.
2. From `hprim.2` we have `¬ ∃ (u) (k), k ≥ 2 ∧ (w ⬝ w) = u ^ k`.
3. We produce a contradiction by exhibiting the existence:
   - `u := w`
   - `k := 2`
   - `h_geq : 2 ≥ 2` (proved by `by norm_num` or `by omega`)
   - `h_eq : w ⬝ w = w ^ 2`
       ```lean4
       calc
         w ⬝ w = w ^ 1 ⬝ w := by rw [Word.pow_one w]
       ```

--- Planning Phase (Iteration 1/3) ---

[PlannerAgent] Reasoning:
The goal is to prove that for any non-empty word `w`, the word `w ⬝ w` has period `w.length`. The definition `HasPeriod (w ⬝ w) w.length` requires two things:

1. `0 < w.length` (positivity of the period).
2. For all indices `i` with `i + w.length < (w ⬝ w).length`, we have `(w ⬝ w).get? i = (w ⬝ w).get? (i + w.length)`.

Condition 1 follows from `hw : w ≠ []` using the lemma `List.length_pos_iff_ne_nil`. For condition 2, we note that `(w ⬝ w).length = w.length + w.length` by `Word.length_concat`. The inequality `i + w.length < w.length + w.length` forces `i < w.length`. Thus `i` lies in the first copy of `w`, while `i + w.length` lies in the second copy. Using the standard list-lemmas `List.get?_append_left` and `List.get?_append_right` (from `Mathlib.Data.List.Basic`) we can compute both sides:

- `(w ⬝ w).get? i = (w ++ w).get? i = w.get? i` (since `i < w.length`).
- `(w ⬝ w).get? (i + w.length) = (w ++ w).get? (i + w.length) = w.get? ((i + w.length) - w.length) = w.get? i` (since `w.length ≤ i + w.length` and `(i + w.length) - w.length = i`).

Thus both sides equal `w.get? i`, establishing the period condition.

The proof is entirely combinatorial, relying only on length arithmetic and the basic properties of list indexing under append.

[PlannerAgent] Plan:
### Step 1: Prove the period is positive
- Use `hw : w ≠ []` and the lemma **`List.length_pos_iff_ne_nil`** to obtain `hpos : 0 < w.length`.
- This gives the first component of `HasPeriod`.

### Step 2: Compute the length of the concatenated word
- Apply **`Word.length_concat`** to get `hlen : (w ⬝ w).length = w.length + w.length`.
- This identity will be used to unfold the length in the index condition.

### Step 3: Take an arbitrary index `i` with the period condition
- Assume `hi : i + w.length < (w ⬝ w).length`.  
- Rewrite using `hlen` to get `i + w.length < w.length + w.length`.
- By `omega` or simple arithmetic, deduce `hi_lt : i < w.length`.

### Step 4: Compute the left‑hand side `(w ⬝ w).get? i`
- Note that `(w ⬝ w) = (w ++ w)` (by definition of `⬝` and `List.append`).
- Using **`List.get?_append_left`** with the condition `hi_lt : i < w.length`,  
  rewrite `(w ++ w).get? i` to `w.get? i`.

### Step 5: Compute the right‑hand side `(w ⬝ w).get? (i + w.length)`
- Observe that `w.length ≤ i + w.length` (trivial because `i` is a natural number).  
  This inequality allows the use of **`List.get?_append_right`**, which yields  
  `(w ++ w).get? (i + w.length) = w.get? ((i + w.length) - w.length)`.
- Simplify `(i + w.length) - w.length` to `i` (using `Nat.add_sub_cancel_left` or `omega`).
- Now the right‑hand side becomes `w.get? i`, which is identical to the left‑hand side.

### Step 6: Conclude the period property
- From Step 4 and Step 5 we have `(w ⬝ w).get? i = (w ⬝ w).get? (i + w.length)`.
- Since `i` was arbitrary, the second component `∀ i, …` is proved.
- Combine with Step 1 to get `HasPeriod (w ⬝ w) w.length`.

### Dependencies
- **Lemmas used:**  
  `Word.length_concat`, `List.length_pos_iff_ne_nil`, `List.get?_append_left`, `List.get?_append_right`.
- **Arithmetic reasoning:** `omega` or `linarith` to handle natural number inequalities and subtraction.

[PlannerAgent] Reasoning:
The original plan was correct in its mathematical essence, but the tactical implementation used by the Builder Agent failed because of incorrect usage of `List.get?_append` (which may not exist in Mathlib 4) and `simp` with conditions. Mathlib 4 provides `List.get?_append_left` and `List.get?_append_right` as the standard lemmas for accessing list elements under concatenation, each with a precise hypothesis. The Builder also attempted `simp [h_not_lt, Nat.add_sub_cancel_left]` inside a `rw` of `List.get?_append`, which is syntactically dubious. We need to formulate a plan that uses the exact lemma names with their required hypotheses, and present the rewriting steps explicitly to avoid ambiguities.

We must prove `HasPeriod (w ⬝ w) w.length`. By definition, `HasPeriod` requires two conditions:

1. `0 < w.length`.
2. For all `i` with `i + w.length < (w ⬝ w).length`, `(w ⬝ w).get? i = (w ⬝ w).get? (i + w.length)`.

Condition 1 follows from `hw : w ≠ []` using the standard Mathlib lemma `List.length_pos_iff_ne_nil`. For condition 2, we fix an arbitrary `i` satisfying the bound. The key observation is that `(w ⬝ w)` is exactly `w ++ w` (as `Word.concat` is `List.append`), and `(w ++ w).length = w.length + w.length` by `Word.length_concat`. Thus the bound `i + w.length < (w ++ w).length` becomes `i + w.length < w.length + w.length`, which forces `i < w.length` (by `omega`). Then:

- The left-hand side `(w ++ w).get? i` can be simplified using `List.get?_append_left` because `i < w.length`. This reduces it to `w.get? i`.
- The right-hand side `(w ++ w).get? (i + w.length)` can be simplified using `List.get?_append_right` because `¬ (i + w.length < w.length)` (which holds because `w.length ≤ i + w.length` by `Nat.le_add_left w.length i`). This reduces it to `w.get? ((i + w.length) - w.length)`. The subtraction simplifies to `i` via `Nat.add_sub_cancel_left`. Hence it also equals `w.get? i`.

Both sides are equal, which completes the proof.

Therefore the mathematical proof remains simple, but we must specify the precise lemmas and the rewrite sequences to avoid tactical errors.

[PlannerAgent] Plan:
### Step 1: Prove the period length is positive
- Use `List.length_pos_iff_ne_nil.mpr hw` to get `hpos : 0 < w.length`.
- This is the first conjunct of `HasPeriod`.

### Step 2: Set up the index condition
- The second conjunct is `∀ i, i + w.length < (w ⬝ w).length → (w ⬝ w).get? i = (w ⬝ w).get? (i + w.length)`.
- Introduce an arbitrary index `i` and assume `hi : i + w.length < (w ⬝ w).length`.

- Use `Word.length_concat` to rewrite `(w ⬝ w).length` as `w.length + w.length`.
- Let `hlen_eq : (w ⬝ w).length = w.length + w.length := by exact Word.length_concat w w`.
- Rewrite `hi` with `hlen_eq` to obtain `hi' : i + w.length < w.length + w.length`.

### Step 4: Derive the key inequality for `i`
- From `hi'` deduce `hi_lt : i < w.length` using the `omega` tactic (or `Nat.lt_of_add_lt_add_left` combined with `Nat.le_add_right`).

### Step 5: Simplify the left-hand side
- Note that `Word.concat` is `List.append`, so `(w ⬝ w).get? i` is `(w ++ w).get? i`.
- Use `List.get?_append_left` which has type `h : i < l₁.length → (l₁ ++ l₂).get? i = l₁.get? i`. Apply it with `h := hi_lt` to get `(w ++ w).get? i = w.get? i`.
- Thus `(w ⬝ w).get? i = w.get? i`.

### Step 6: Simplify the right-hand side
- For the index `i + w.length`, we need to apply `List.get?_append_right`, which requires `¬ i + w.length < w.length`.
- This condition is true because `w.length ≤ i + w.length` (by `Nat.le_add_left w.length i`). Using `Nat.not_lt.mpr` with `Nat.le_add_left w.length i` (or `Nat.le_of_lt?`) we get `h_not_lt : ¬ i + w.length < w.length`.
- Then `List.get?_append_right h_not_lt` gives `(w ++ w).get? (i + w.length) = w.get? ((i + w.length) - w.length)`.
- Simplify the subtraction: `(i + w.length) - w.length = i` using `Nat.add_sub_cancel_left` (or `Nat.add_sub_cancel`).
- Thus `(w ++ w).get? (i + w.length) = w.get? i`.

### Step 7: Conclude equality and assemble the proof
- From Steps 5 and 6, both sides equal `w.get? i`, so they are equal.
- Since `i` was arbitrary, the universal quantifier is satisfied.
- Combine with `hpos` to give `HasPeriod (w ⬝ w) w.length`.

- `List.length_pos_iff_ne_nil` (from Mathlib/Data/List/Basic)

- `List.get?_append_right` (Mathlib, type: `h : ¬ i < l₁.length → (l₁ ++ l₂).get? i = l₂.get? (i - l₁.length)`)

```lean4
    refine Nat.pos_of_ne_zero (fun hzero => hw ?_)
    exact List.length_eq_zero.mp hzero

  have h_not_lt : ¬ (i + w.length < w.length) := by omega

      rw [List.get?_append]
      exact if_neg h_not_lt
    _ = (w ⬝ w).get? (i + w.length) := rfl
```

[PlannerAgent] Reasoning:
The mathematical reasoning remains correct: we need to show that for any non-empty word `w`, the concatenation `w ++ w` has period `|w|`. The previous Builder attempts failed because they used `List.get?_append` (a conditional rewriting lemma) with `if_pos`/`if_neg`, which is not the idiomatic approach in Lean 4. Mathlib 4 provides the simplifying lemmas `List.get?_append_left` and `List.get?_append_right` that directly rewrite the goal under the appropriate hypotheses. Our plan will explictly instruct using these lemmas via `rw` to avoid the conditional splitting. We also need to be precise about the arithmetic: derive `i < w.length` from the index bound, then apply the left lemma; derive `¬ (i + w.length < w.length)` (or `w.length ≤ i + w.length`) for the right lemma.

Since the Builder may not be aware of the exact statement of `List.get?_append_right`, we will mention that it requires a proof of `l₁.length ≤ i` rather than `¬ i < l₁.length`. We obtain this from `Nat.le_of_not_lt h_not_lt`. The subtraction `Nat.add_sub_cancel_right` simplifies the index correctly. The plan remains essentially the same but with explicit lemma names and `rw` directions.

[PlannerAgent] Plan:
### Step 1: Prove the period is positive
- From `hw : w ≠ []` we obtain `0 < w.length` using `List.length_pos_iff_ne_nil.mpr hw`. Name this `hpos`.
- This gives the first conjunct of `HasPeriod`.

### Step 2: Set up the index condition
- The second conjunct is `∀ i, i + w.length < (w ⬝ w).length → (w ⬝ w).get? i = (w ⬝ w).get? (i + w.length)`.
- Introduce an arbitrary index `i` and hypothesis `hi : i + w.length < (w ⬝ w).length`.

### Step 3: Rewrite the length of the concatenated word
- Use `have hlen : (w ⬝ w).length = w.length + w.length := Word.length_concat w w`.
- Rewrite `hi` using `hlen` to obtain `hi' : i + w.length < w.length + w.length`.

### Step 4: Derive auxiliary arithmetic facts
- From `hi'` deduce `hi_lt : i < w.length` by `omega` (or `Nat.lt_of_add_lt_add_left`).
- Also deduce `h_not_lt : ¬ (i + w.length < w.length)` using `omega`. Convert this to `h_le : w.length ≤ i + w.length` using `Nat.le_of_not_lt h_not_lt`. (This will be used for the right lemma.)

### Step 5: Simplify the left-hand side
- Observe that `(w ⬝ w).get? i` is `(w ++ w).get? i` (since `⬝` is `++`).
- Use `rw [List.get?_append_left hi_lt]` to rewrite to `w.get? i`.

### Step 6: Simplify the right-hand side
- For `(w ++ w).get? (i + w.length)` we have `h_le : w.length ≤ i + w.length`.
- Use `rw [List.get?_append_right h_le]` to obtain `w.get? ((i + w.length) - w.length)`.
- Simplify the index: `(i + w.length) - w.length = i` by `Nat.add_sub_cancel_right`.
- Then `rw [Nat.add_sub_cancel_right]` yields `w.get? i`.

### Step 7: Conclude equality
- Steps 5 and 6 show both sides equal `w.get? i`. Hence `(w ⬝ w).get? i = (w ⬝ w).get? (i + w.length)`.
- Since `i` was arbitrary, the universal condition is proved.
- Together with `hpos`, we obtain `HasPeriod (w ⬝ w) w.length`.

### Exact lemma names used
- `List.length_pos_iff_ne_nil` : `0 < length l ↔ l ≠ []`
- `Word.length_concat` : `(u ⬝ v).length = u.length + v.length`
- `List.get?_append_left` : `(h : i < l₁.length) → (l₁ ++ l₂).get? i = l₁.get? i`
- `List.get?_append_right` : `(h : l₁.length ≤ i) → (l₁ ++ l₂).get? i = l₂.get? (i - l₁.length)`
- `Nat.add_sub_cancel_right` : `(a + b) - b = a`
- `Nat.le_of_not_lt` : `¬ a < b → b ≤ a`

--- Planning Phase (Iteration 1/3) ---

[PlannerAgent] Reasoning:
We need to prove that if a word `w` has period `p` (with `0 < p`), then `w` also has period `k * p` for any `k ≥ 1`. The definition of `HasPeriod w (k * p)` requires two things:

1. `0 < k * p`.
2. For all indices `i` with `i + k * p < w.length`, we have `w.get? i = w.get? (i + k * p)`.

Condition 1 is immediate from `hp.1 : 0 < p` and `hk : 1 ≤ k` (hence `0 < k`), using `mul_pos`.

Condition 2 is the core of the proof. Since `p` is a period, adding a single `p` preserves the letter at index `i` whenever the resulting index is within bounds. Adding `k` copies of `p` can be achieved by repeatedly applying the `p`-periodicity `k` times. More formally, we can prove by induction on `n` (for natural numbers `n`) that for any `i` with `i + n * p < w.length`, we have `w.get? i = w.get? (i + n * p)`. The base case `n = 0` is trivial. For the induction step, assume the property holds for `n = m`, and we have `i + (m+1) * p < w.length`. Then certainly `i + m * p < w.length` (because `(m+1)*p = m*p + p ≥ m*p`), so by the induction hypothesis `w.get? i = w.get? (i + m * p)`. Now we can apply `hp.2` at index `i + m * p` because `(i + m * p) + p = i + (m+1)*p` and the given bound ensures this is `< w.length`. This yields `w.get? (i + m * p) = w.get? ((i + m * p) + p) = w.get? (i + (m+1)*p)`. Combining these equalities gives the desired result for `n = m+1`. Applying this lemma with `n := k` to the original index `i` and the given bound completes the proof.

The proof uses only basic arithmetic (`ring` and `omega`) and the `HasPeriod` hypothesis. No external list lemmas beyond those already present are needed.

[PlannerAgent] Plan:
### Step 1: Extract positivity of `p`
- From `hp : HasPeriod w p` we have `hp.1 : 0 < p`.

### Step 2: Prove that the new period `k * p` is positive
- Since `hk : 1 ≤ k`, we have `0 < k` (by `omega`). Combine with `hp.1` using `mul_pos` to get `0 < k * p`. This supplies the first condition of `HasPeriod`.

### Step 3: Set up the main equality condition
- The second condition requires: for any `i` with `i + k * p < w.length`, `w.get? i = w.get? (i + k * p)`.
- Introduce an arbitrary index `i` and hypothesis `hi : i + k * p < w.length`.

### Step 4: Prove a general lemma by induction on `n`
- State and prove the auxiliary lemma: `∀ n : ℕ, i + n * p < w.length → w.get? i = w.get? (i + n * p)`.
  - **Base case** `n = 0`: `i + 0 * p = i`, so the equality is trivial.
  - **Inductive step**: assume the lemma holds for `n = m`, and we need to prove it for `n = m + 1`.
    - Given `hm1 : i + (m+1)*p < w.length`, derive `hm0 : i + m * p < w.length`. This follows because `m * p ≤ (m+1)*p` (since `p > 0`), so `i + m*p ≤ i + (m+1)*p < w.length`.
    - Apply the induction hypothesis `hm0` to get `w.get? i = w.get? (i + m * p)`.
    - Apply `hp.2` (the periodicity condition) at index `j := i + m * p`. For this we need the hypothesis `(i + m * p) + p < w.length`. But this is exactly `hm1` after rewriting `(i + m * p) + p = i + (m + 1)*p` using `ring`.
    - This yields `w.get? (i + m * p) = w.get? ((i + m * p) + p) = w.get? (i + (m+1)*p)`.
    - Concatenating the equalities gives the result for `n = m + 1`.

### Step 5: Apply the auxiliary lemma with `n := k`
- Instantiate the lemma with `n := k` and the hypothesis `hi` (which matches `i + k * p < w.length`) to obtain exactly `w.get? i = w.get? (i + k * p)`.
- This proves the universal condition for the given `i`. Since `i` was arbitrary, the `∀` quantifier is satisfied.

### Step 6: Combine to form the final `HasPeriod` statement
- Provide `⟨hpos, λ i hi => h_induction k hi⟩` (where `h_induction` is the aux lemma specialized to `k`).

### Exact lemmas used
- `hp.1` (positivity of `p`)
- `mul_pos` (from `Mathlib.Tactic` or `Nat`; `mul_pos` requires `0 < k` and `0 < p`)
- `hp.2` (the periodicity condition: `∀ i : ℕ, i + p < w.length → w.get? i = w.get? (i + p)`)
- `ring` tactic to rewrite multiplicative expressions like `(m+1)*p = m*p + p`.
- `omega` for arithmetic inequalities (`i + m*p ≤ i + (m+1)*p` and deriving `i + m*p < w.length` from `i + (m+1)*p < w.length`).
- `simp` for the base case `n = 0`.

--- Planning Phase (Iteration 2/3) ---

[PlannerAgent] Reasoning:
The goal is to show that if a word `w` has period `p` (with `0 < p`), then for any multiplier `k ≥ 1`, `w` also has period `k·p`. The definition `HasPeriod w (k·p)` requires:

1. `0 < k·p`,
2. For all indices `i` with `i + k·p < w.length`, we have `w.get? i = w.get? (i + k·p)`.

Condition 1 follows from the positivity of `p` (given by `hp.1`) and the fact that `k ≥ 1` ensures `0 < k`, hence the product is positive via `Nat.mul_pos`.

Condition 2 is proved by induction on the multiplier `n`. The induction hypothesis is that for any `i` with `i + n·p < w.length`, the equality holds. For the step from `n` to `n+1`, given `i + (n+1)·p < w.length` we note:

- `(n+1)·p = n·p + p` (by `Nat.succ_mul`), so the hypothesis becomes `i + (n·p + p) < w.length`.
- Because `p > 0`, we have `i + n·p ≤ i + (n·p + p)`, hence `i + n·p < w.length`.
- The induction hypothesis applied at the same index `i` gives `w.get? i = w.get? (i + n·p)`.
- The original periodicity of `w` (from `hp`) can be used at index `j = i + n·p`: we need `(i + n·p) + p < w.length`, which is exactly `i + (n·p + p) < w.length`, i.e., the current hypothesis after rewriting.
- Applying `hp.2` gives `w.get? (i + n·p) = w.get? ((i + n·p) + p) = w.get? (i + (n·p + p)) = w.get? (i + (n+1)·p)`.
- Concatenating the equalities yields the desired equality for `n+1`.

All arithmetic steps (inequalities and rewriting of sums) can be handled by the `omega` tactic, which is robust for linear arithmetic in `ℕ`. We will avoid `ring` and instead rely on `omega` and the basic lemma `Nat.succ_mul` to simplify the multiplicative terms.

[PlannerAgent] Plan:
### Step 1: Extract the positivity condition from the hypothesis
- Let `hp_pos : 0 < p := hp.1`.

### Step 2: Obtain positivity of `k` from `hk : 1 ≤ k`
- `hk_pos : 0 < k := by omega`.

### Step 3: Prove `0 < k * p` (first conjunct of `HasPeriod`)
- `hpos : 0 < k * p := Nat.mul_pos hk_pos hp_pos`.

### Step 4: Prove the index‑equality condition by induction on the multiplier `n`
- Define a helper lemma `lemma aux (n : ℕ) : ∀ i, i + n * p < w.length → w.get? i = w.get? (i + n * p) :=` by induction on `n`.

**Base case `n = 0`**:
  - The goal reduces to `∀ i, i + 0 < w.length → w.get? i = w.get? (i + 0)`. Simplify with `simp` (or `omega`).

**Inductive step**: Assume `aux n` holds, prove `aux (n+1)`.
  - Fix an arbitrary index `i` and assume `hi : i + (n+1)*p < w.length`.
  - Rewrite `(n+1)*p` as `n*p + p` using `Nat.succ_mul n p`. The hypothesis becomes `hi' : i + (n*p + p) < w.length`.
  - Derive the bound for `n`:  
    Show `i + n*p < w.length`.  
    Because `p > 0` we have `i + n*p ≤ i + (n*p + p)`. Using `hi'` and this inequality, `omega` yields `h_bound_n : i + n*p < w.length`.
  - Apply the induction hypothesis `aux n i h_bound_n` to obtain `heq1 : w.get? i = w.get? (i + n*p)`.
  - Prepare the argument for `hp.2` at index `j := i + n*p`.  
    Need to show `j + p < w.length`.  
    Compute `j + p = (i + n*p) + p = i + (n*p + p)`, which is exactly the left‑hand side of `hi'`. So we reuse `hi'` to get `h_bound_p : j + p < w.length`.
  - Apply `hp.2 j h_bound_p` to get `heq2 : w.get? (j) = w.get? (j + p)`.
  - Chain the equalities:  
    `w.get? i = w.get? (i + n*p)` (by `heq1`)  
    `= w.get? ((i + n*p) + p)` (by `heq2`)  
    `= w.get? (i + (n*p + p))` (by associativity)  
    `= w.get? (i + (n+1)*p)` (by `Nat.succ_mul` again).
  - All arithmetic rewrites inside the chain can be performed with `rw` and `omega` or `simp [Nat.succ_mul, add_assoc]`.

### Step 5: Instantiate the auxiliary lemma with `n := k`
- `h_periodic : ∀ i, i + k * p < w.length → w.get? i = w.get? (i + k * p) := aux k`.

### Step 6: Combine everything to obtain `HasPeriod w (k * p)`
- `exact ⟨hpos, h_periodic⟩`

### Key lemmas used
- `hp.1` : `0 < p`
- `Nat.mul_pos hk_pos hp_pos` : `0 < k * p`
- `Nat.succ_mul n p` : `(n+1)*p = n*p + p`  (from Mathlib/Data/Nat/Basic)
- `hp.2` : periodicity condition `∀ i, i + p < w.length → w.get? i = w.get? (i + p)`
- `omega` tactic for all linear arithmetic inequalities and equality simplifications.
- `simp` for the base case.

--- Planning Phase (Iteration 3/3) ---

[PlannerAgent] Reasoning:
We need to prove `HasPeriod w (k * p)` given `hp : HasPeriod w p` and `hk : 1 ≤ k`. The definition consists of positivity `0 < k * p` and a universal condition on indices. The earlier attempts used an induction on `k` that mixed the fixed parameter `k` with the goal’s lambda binder, which is error‑prone. A cleaner strategy is to prove a general lemma by induction on `n : ℕ`:

`lemma period_mul (n : ℕ) : ∀ i, i + n * p < w.length → w.get? i = w.get? (i + n * p) := …`

Then instantiate `period_mul k` to obtain the required condition. The induction is straightforward: base case `n = 0` is trivial; the inductive step uses `Nat.succ_mul` to rewrite the target multiplier, the induction hypothesis for `n`, and the original periodicity from `hp` at the shifted index. All arithmetic inequalities and equalities can be dispatched with `omega`, avoiding fragile `ring` or `simp` combinations.

[PlannerAgent] Plan:
### Step 1: Extract hypotheses
- Let `hp_pos : 0 < p := hp.1`.
- Let `hk_pos : 0 < k` from `hk` by `omega`.
- Positivity of the new period: `hpos : 0 < k * p := Nat.mul_pos hk_pos hp_pos`.

### Step 2: Prove a helper lemma by induction on `n`
Define
```
lemma period_mul (n : ℕ) : ∀ i, i + n * p < w.length → w.get? i = w.get? (i + n * p) := by
  induction' n with n ih
  · intro i hi; simp
  · intro i hi
    have hi' : i + (n * p + p) < w.length := by
      -- using Nat.succ_mul
      simpa [Nat.succ_mul] using hi
    have h_bound_n : i + n * p < w.length := by
      -- because p > 0, n*p < n*p + p → i + n*p < i + (n*p + p)
      omega
    have heq1 : w.get? i = w.get? (i + n * p) := ih i h_bound_n
    have h_bound_p : (i + n * p) + p < w.length := by
      -- (i + n * p) + p = i + (n * p + p), which is exactly hi'
      simpa [add_assoc] using hi'
    have heq2 : w.get? (i + n * p) = w.get? ((i + n * p) + p) :=
      hp.2 (i + n * p) h_bound_p
    rw [heq1, heq2]
    congr 1
    omega
```
- **Base case `n = 0`**: `i + 0 * p = i`, so `simp` closes the goal.
- **Inductive step**:
  1. Rewrite the hypothesis `hi` (which is `i + (n+1)*p < w.length`) using `Nat.succ_mul` to `i + (n * p + p) < w.length`; call this `hi'`.
  2. Derive `h_bound_n : i + n * p < w.length` using `omega`, leveraging `hp_pos` to know `n*p < n*p + p`.
  3. Apply the induction hypothesis `ih` at the same index `i` with `h_bound_n` to get `heq1`.
  4. The original periodicity `hp.2` needs the hypothesis `(i + n * p) + p < w.length`. Show this by rewriting `(i + n * p) + p` to `i + (n * p + p)` via associativity and using `hi'`. This yields `h_bound_p` via `simpa [add_assoc]`.
  5. Apply `hp.2` to obtain `heq2`.
  6. `rw` both equalities into the goal.
  7. The remaining equality `(i + n * p) + p = i + (n+1) * p` is a pure arithmetic identity; `omega` solves it.

### Step 3: Instantiate the lemma with `n := k`
- `have h_periodic : ∀ i, i + k * p < w.length → w.get? i = w.get? (i + k * p) := period_mul k`.

### Step 4: Combine into `HasPeriod`
- `exact ⟨hpos, h_periodic⟩`

### Key lemmas used
- `hp.1`, `hp.2`
- `Nat.mul_pos`
- `Nat.succ_mul n p` : `(n+1)*p = n*p + p`
- `add_assoc` for rewriting parentheses
- `omega` tactic for all linear arithmetic inequalities and equality of `Nat` expressions.

--- Planning Phase (Iteration 1/3) ---

[PlannerAgent] Reasoning:
We are given `hp : HasPeriod w p`, `hpre : u ≤ₚ w`, and `hlen : p ≤ u.length`. We must prove `HasPeriod u p`. The definition of `HasPeriod` consists of `0 < p` and the index condition:

`∀ i, i + p < u.length → u.get? i = u.get? (i + p)`.

From `hp` we immediately have `0 < p`, so the first part is done. For the second part, take an arbitrary index `i` with `hi : i + p < u.length`. The idea is to relate `u` to `w` using the prefix property, then apply `hp.2` at the same index `i` in `w`.

Since `hpre : u ≤ₚ w`, we can use `IsPrefix.def` to obtain a `v` such that `w = u ++ v` (or equivalently `w = u ⬝ v`). This decomposition allows us to connect positions in `u` to positions in `w` via `List.get?_append_left`:

- Because `i < u.length` (from `hi` and `hlen` or directly from `i + p < u.length` we get `i < u.length`), we have `(u ++ v).get? i = u.get? i`. Hence `w.get? i = u.get? i`.
- Similarly, from `i + p < u.length` we have `(u ++ v).get? (i + p) = u.get? (i + p)`, giving `w.get? (i + p) = u.get? (i + p)`.

Now we need to apply the periodicity of `w` at index `i`. The required hypothesis is `i + p < w.length`. Since `u ++ v = w`, we have `w.length = u.length + v.length` (by `Word.length_concat` or `List.length_append`). Because `i + p < u.length`, we trivially get `i + p < w.length` (as `u.length ≤ u.length + v.length`). More formally, we can use `omega` or `Nat.lt_of_lt_of_le` with `hi` and `IsPrefix.length_le hpre` (which gives `u.length ≤ w.length`).

Applying `hp.2 i` with the bound `i + p < w.length` yields `w.get? i = w.get? (i + p)`. Substituting the equalities from the prefix decomposition gives `u.get? i = u.get? (i + p)`. This completes the universal condition.

All steps are purely combinatorial, using only the provided lemmas from the CoW library and standard list lemmas.

[PlannerAgent] Plan:
### Step 1: Extract positivity of `p`
- From `hp : HasPeriod w p` take `hp_pos : 0 < p := hp.1`.
- This satisfies the first condition of `HasPeriod u p`.

### Step 2: Use the prefix hypothesis to decompose `w`
- Apply `IsPrefix.def u w` to `hpre` to obtain a suffix `v` and an equality `hw_eq : w = u ++ v` (or `w = u ⬝ v`, but we'll use `List.append` form). The lemma `IsPrefix.def` gives `∃ v, w = u ++ v`.
- Let `⟨v, hw_eq⟩ := (IsPrefix.def u w).mp hpre`.

### Step 3: Relate lengths
- Compute `h_len_pre : u.length ≤ w.length` using `IsPrefix.length_le hpre`.
- From `hw_eq` we also have `Word.length_concat u v` giving `w.length = u.length + v.length`, but the inequality is sufficient.

### Step 4: Introduce an arbitrary index `i` with the bound
- For the second condition, we need: `∀ i, i + p < u.length → u.get? i = u.get? (i + p)`.
- Fix `i : ℕ` and assume `hi : i + p < u.length`.

### Step 5: Derive auxiliary inequalities
- From `hi` we have `i_lt_u : i < u.length` by `omega`.
- Also `i_plus_p_lt_u : i + p < u.length` is exactly `hi`.
- Combine with `h_len_pre` to get `hi_w : i + p < w.length` using `omega` (or `Nat.lt_of_lt_of_le hi h_len_pre`).

### Step 6: Connect `u` elements to `w` elements
- Since `w = u ++ v`, we can use `List.get?_append_left` (which needs `i < u.length` or `i+p < u.length`).
  - `have hu_i : u.get? i = (u ++ v).get? i := by rw [List.get?_append_left i_lt_u]`. But this rewrites the wrong direction; better: `calc u.get? i = (u ++ v).get? i := by rw [List.get?_append_left i_lt_u] ... = w.get? i := by rw [hw_eq]`.
  - Similarly, `hu_ip : u.get? (i + p) = w.get? (i + p)` because `i + p < u.length`.
- The explicit rewriting:
  - `have h_left : w.get? i = u.get? i := by rw [hw_eq, List.get?_append_left i_lt_u]`
  - `have h_right : w.get? (i + p) = u.get? (i + p) := by rw [hw_eq, List.get?_append_left hi]` (note: `hi` is `i+p < u.length`, which is exactly the condition).

### Step 7: Apply the periodicity of `w`
- `hp.2 i hi_w` gives `w.get? i = w.get? (i + p)`.
- Combine: `u.get? i = w.get? i` (by `h_left`), `w.get? i = w.get? (i + p)` (by `hp.2`), and `w.get? (i + p) = u.get? (i + p)` (by `h_right`). Therefore `u.get? i = u.get? (i + p)`.

### Step 8: Conclude `HasPeriod u p`
- Return `⟨hp_pos, λ i hi => ...⟩` with the chain of equalities.

### Key lemmas used
- `hp.1`, `hp.2`
- `IsPrefix.def`, `IsPrefix.length_le`
- `Word.length_concat` (optional, only if we need the exact length equality; the inequality `u.length ≤ w.length` from `IsPrefix.length_le` is enough)
- `List.get?_append_left` : `(l₁ ++ l₂).get? i = l₁.get? i` when `i < l₁.length`
- `omega` for arithmetic reasoning

--- Planning Phase (Iteration 2/3) ---

[PlannerAgent] Reasoning:
Our earlier plan used `List.get?_append_left` which may not be present or may have a different name in Mathlib4. We can avoid it entirely by relating `u` to `w` via `List.take` and using the standard lemma `List.get?_take`. The prefix hypothesis `hpre` gives `w = u ++ v` for some `v`. Then `w.take u.length = u` by `List.take_append`. For any index `i < u.length`, `List.get?_take` allows us to connect `u.get? i` to `w.get? i`. This approach uses only widely available, robust lemmas.

<plan>
### Step 1: Extract positivity of `p`
- `hp_pos : 0 < p := hp.1`.

### Step 2: Decompose `w` using the prefix
- Use `IsPrefix.def` to get `⟨v, hw⟩` with `hw : w = u ++ v`.
- Example: `rcases (IsPrefix.def u w).mp hpre with ⟨v, hw⟩`.

### Step 3: Prove `w.take u.length = u`
- Compute:
  ```
  have h_take : w.take u.length = u := by
    rw [hw]
    exact (List.take_append u v).symm   -- (u ++ v).take u.length = u
  ```
  (Check: `List.take_append l₁ l₂ : (l₁ ++ l₂).take l₁.length = l₁`. This lemma exists in Mathlib4.)

### Step 4: Set up the index condition
- The goal is `∀ i, i + p < u.length → u.get? i = u.get? (i + p)`.
- Fix `i` and assume `hi : i + p < u.length`.

### Step 5: Derive auxiliary index bounds
- `hi_i : i < u.length` (by `omega`).
- `hi_ip : i + p < u.length` is exactly `hi`.
- `hi_w : i + p < w.length`:
  - From `hpre` we have `h_len_pre : u.length ≤ w.length` via `IsPrefix.length_le hpre`.
  - Then `i + p < u.length ≤ w.length`, so `omega` gives `hi_w`.

### Step 6: Relate `u.get? i` to `w.get? i`
- Using `h_take` and `List.get?_take`.
  ```
  have hui : u.get? i = w.get? i := by
    calc
      u.get? i = (w.take u.length).get? i := by rw [h_take]
      _ = w.get? i := by rw [List.get?_take hi_i]
  ```

### Step 7: Relate `u.get? (i + p)` to `w.get? (i + p)`
- Similarly,
  ```
  have huip : u.get? (i + p) = w.get? (i + p) := by
    calc
      u.get? (i + p) = (w.take u.length).get? (i + p) := by rw [h_take]
      _ = w.get? (i + p) := by rw [List.get?_take hi_ip]
  ```

### Step 8: Use the periodicity of `w`
- From `hp` we have `hp_per : ∀ i, i + p < w.length → w.get? i = w.get? (i + p)` (this is `hp.2`).
- Apply `hp.2 i hi_w` to get `h_w_period : w.get? i = w.get? (i + p)`.

### Step 9: Chain equalities
- `calc
    u.get? i = w.get? i := hui
    _ = w.get? (i + p) := h_w_period
    _ = u.get? (i + p) := by rw [huip]
  `

### Step 10: Assemble the final statement
- `refine ⟨hp_pos, ?_⟩`
- Then provide the function constructed in Steps 4–9.
