```lean4
    intro m
    induction' m with k ih
    · intro j hj; exfalso; simpa using hj
    · intro j hj
      rw [Word.pow_succ w k]
      rw [List.get?_append]
      have hlen_k : (w ^ k).length = k * w.length := Word.length_pow w k
      have h_succ_length : (w ^ (k+1)).length = (w ^ k).length + w.length := by
        rw [Word.pow_succ, Word.length_concat]
      rw [h_succ_length] at hj
      rw [hlen_k] at hj
      by_cases h : j < (w ^ k).length
      · rw [if_pos h]
        exact ih j h
      · rw [if_neg h]
        have hge : (w ^ k).length ≤ j := by omega
        rw [hlen_k] at hge
        set r := j - k * w.length with hr
        have hr_lt : r < w.length := by omega
        have hsub_eq : j - (w ^ k).length = r := by
          rw [hlen_k]
          rfl
        have hmod_eq : j % w.length = r := by
          have hj_eq : j = k * w.length + r := by omega
          rw [hj_eq]
          calc
            (k * w.length + r) % w.length = ((k * w.length) % w.length + r % w.length) % w.length := by rw [Nat.add_mod]
            _ = (0 + r % w.length) % w.length := by rw [Nat.mul_mod_right]
            _ = r % w.length := by simp
            _ = r := Nat.mod_eq_of_lt hr_lt
        rw [hsub_eq, hmod_eq]
  have hi_len : i < (w ^ (n+1)).length := by
    have : i ≤ i + w.length := by omega
    omega
  rw [h_mod (n+1) i hi_len, h_mod (n+1) (i + w.length) hi]
  simp [Nat.add_mod_right]
```

```lean4
have hpos : 0 < w.length := List.length_pos_iff_ne_nil.mpr hw
  have get_pow_mul_add (m q r : ℕ) (hq : q < m) (hr : r < w.length) : (w ^ m).get? (q * w.length + r) = w.get? r := by
    induction' m with k ih generalizing q
    · exact absurd hq (Nat.not_lt_zero _)
    · rw [Word.pow_succ]
      have hlen : (w ^ k).length = k * w.length := Word.length_pow w k
      rw [List.get?_append, hlen]
      by_cases hqk : q < k
      · have h_lt : q * w.length + r < k * w.length := by
          have h1 : q * w.length + r < (q + 1) * w.length := by
            calc
              q * w.length + r < q * w.length + w.length := Nat.add_lt_add_left hr _
              _ = (q + 1) * w.length := by ring
          have h2 : (q + 1) * w.length ≤ k * w.length :=
            Nat.mul_le_mul_right (w.length) (Nat.succ_le_of_lt hqk)
          exact lt_of_lt_of_le h1 h2
        rw [if_pos h_lt]
        exact ih q hqk hr
      · have hq_le_k : q ≤ k := Nat.le_of_lt_succ hq
        have hk_le_q : k ≤ q := Nat.le_of_not_gt hqk
        have hq_eq_k : q = k := Nat.le_antisymm hq_le_k hk_le_q
        subst hq_eq_k
        have h_ge : ¬ (k * w.length + r < k * w.length) :=
          Nat.not_lt.mpr (Nat.le_add_right _ _)
        rw [if_neg h_ge]
        simp [Nat.add_sub_cancel_left]
  refine ⟨hpos, λ i hi => ?_⟩
  rw [Word.length_pow w (n + 1)] at hi
  rw [Nat.succ_mul] at hi
  have hi_lt_n : i < n * w.length := Nat.lt_of_add_lt_add_right hi
  set q := i / w.length with hq_def
  set r := i % w.length with hr_def
  have h_eq : i = q * w.length + r := Nat.div_add_mod i w.length
  have hr_lt : r < w.length := Nat.mod_lt i hpos
  have h_mul_lt : q * w.length < n * w.length := by
    calc
      q * w.length ≤ q * w.length + r := Nat.le_add_right _ _
      _ = i := by rw [← h_eq]
      _ < n * w.length := hi_lt_n
  have hq_lt_n : q < n := (Nat.mul_lt_mul_right hpos).mp h_mul_lt
  have hq_lt_np1 : q < n + 1 := Nat.lt_succ_of_lt hq_lt_n
  have hq_succ_lt_np1 : q + 1 < n + 1 := Nat.add_lt_add_right hq_lt_n 1
  rw [h_eq]
  rw [show (q * w.length + r) + w.length = (q + 1) * w.length + r by ring]
  rw [get_pow_mul_add (n + 1) q r hq_lt_np1 hr_lt]
  rw [get_pow_mul_add (n + 1) (q + 1) r hq_succ_lt_np1 hr_lt]
```

--- Planning Phase (Iteration 2/3) ---

[PlannerAgent] Reasoning:
The theorem `hasPeriod_pow_length` asserts that for a non‑empty word `w`, the power `w^(n+1)` has period `|w|`. The period condition is an equality of list entries at indices `i` and `i+|w|`. The key observation is that in `w^(n+1)`, any index `i` can be reduced modulo `|w|` to get the same entry as in the base word `w`. More precisely, for any `i < (n+1)·|w|`, we have `(w^(n+1)).get? i = w.get? (i % |w|)`. Once this is established, adding `|w|` to `i` does not change the remainder, so the equality follows immediately.

The previous Builder attempt built a complicated helper `get_pow_mul_add` using division and quotient representation, which made the proof brittle. A better approach is to prove the modular reduction lemma directly by induction on `n`, using the concatenation structure of powers (`Word.pow_succ`) and the length formula (`Word.length_pow`). The induction splits into two cases: whether the index lies in the first `n+1` copies or in the final copy. Both cases rewrite with `List.get?_append_left` or `List.get?_append_right` and then apply the induction hypothesis or a simple remainder identity. All arithmetic is handled by `omega`, avoiding manual `ring`. Finally the main theorem applies the modular lemma to both `i` and `i+|w|` and uses `Nat.add_mod_right` to equate the remainders.

[PlannerAgent] Plan:
### Step 1: Prove `0 < w.length`
- Use `List.length_pos_iff_ne_nil.mpr hw` to get `hpos : 0 < w.length`.
- This is the first component of `HasPeriod`.

### Step 2: Prove the modular-access lemma
- Define and prove a helper lemma:
  ```
  lemma pow_get?_mod (w : Word α) (n : ℕ) (i : ℕ) (hi : i < (n+1) * w.length) :
    (w ^ (n+1)).get? i = w.get? (i % w.length) :=
  ```
- Proof by induction on `n`.

  **Base case `n = 0`:**
  - `w ^ 1 = w` by `Word.pow_one`.
  - Then `hi` becomes `i < w.length`. Hence `i % w.length = i` by `Nat.mod_eq_of_lt hi`.
  - `simp [Word.pow_one, hi, Nat.mod_eq_of_lt hi]`.

  **Inductive step `n → n+1`:**
  - Assume the lemma holds for `n`. Show for `s_n := n+1`.
  - `w ^ ((n+1)+1) = w ^ (n+1) ⬝ w` by `Word.pow_succ`.
  - Let `h_len_pow : (w ^ (n+1)).length = (n+1) * w.length` by `Word.length_pow w (n+1)`.
  - Given `hi' : i < ((n+1)+1) * w.length` (which is `(n+2)*w.length`).

  **Case split on whether `i` is inside the first `n+1` copies:**
  - `by_cases h_lt : i < (n+1) * w.length`
    * **If `h_lt`:**  
      - `(w ^ (n+1) ⬝ w).get? i = (w ^ (n+1)).get? i` by `List.get?_append_left` (using `h_len_pow` to match the index bound).  
      - Apply the induction hypothesis `pow_get?_mod w n i h_lt` to rewrite to `w.get? (i % w.length)`. Done.
    * **Otherwise `h_ge : (n+1) * w.length ≤ i`:**
      - Set `j := i - (n+1) * w.length`.  
      - Derive `h_j_lt : j < w.length` from `hi'` and `h_ge` using `omega`.  
      - `(w ^ (n+1) ⬝ w).get? i = w.get? j` by `List.get?_append_right` with `h_len_pow ▸ h_ge`.  
      - Need to show `w.get? j = w.get? (i % w.length)`.  
        * Show `i % w.length = j`.  
          Because `i = (n+1) * w.length + j` (by `omega`), and `j < w.length`.  
          Hence `i % w.length = j % w.length = j` by `Nat.mod_eq_of_lt`.  
        * `rw` this equivalence, and the goal becomes `w.get? j = w.get? j`.  
      - All arithmetic in this branch can be handled with `omega`, especially `rw` of the equality and `Nat.mod_eq_of_lt`.

### Step 3: Apply the modular lemma to the main theorem
- The second component of `HasPeriod` is
  ```
  ∀ i, i + w.length < (w ^ (n+1)).length → (w ^ (n+1)).get? i = (w ^ (n+1)).get? (i + w.length)
  ```
- Introduce `i` and `hi` as hypothesis.
- Compute `h_len : (w ^ (n+1)).length = (n+1) * w.length` via `Word.length_pow w (n+1)`.
- Rewrite `hi` using `h_len` to get `hi' : i + w.length < (n+1) * w.length`.
- From `hi'` we immediately have both `i < (n+1) * w.length` and `i + w.length < (n+1) * w.length` (by `omega`). Call them `hi_i` and `hi_ip`.

- Apply `pow_get?_mod w n i hi_i` to obtain `h1 : (w ^ (n+1)).get? i = w.get? (i % w.length)`.
- Apply `pow_get?_mod w n (i + w.length) hi_ip` to obtain `h2 : (w ^ (n+1)).get? (i + w.length) = w.get? ((i + w.length) % w.length)`.

- Note that `(i + w.length) % w.length = i % w.length` by the lemma `Nat.add_mod_right` (or `Nat.mod_add_cancel`). Use `simp [Nat.add_mod_right]` to rewrite.
- Therefore `h2` rewrites to `w.get? (i % w.length)`.
- Conclude `h1 = h2`, giving the needed equality.

### Step 4: Assemble the final `HasPeriod`
- `exact ⟨hpos, λ i hi => …⟩` using the chain above.

### Key lemmas referenced
- `List.length_pos_iff_ne_nil` (Mathlib)
- `Word.pow_succ` (CoW.Word)
- `Word.length_pow` (CoW.Word)
- `List.get?_append_left` (Mathlib)
- `List.get?_append_right` (Mathlib)
- `Nat.mod_eq_of_lt` (Mathlib)
- `Nat.add_mod_right` (Mathlib)
- `omega` tactic for all arithmetic reasoning.

```lean4
  have pow_get_mod (k : ℕ) (i : ℕ) (hi : i < (k + 1) * w.length) : (w ^ (k + 1)).get? i = w.get? (i % w.length) := by
    revert i
    induction' k with k ih
    · intro i hi
      have hi' : i < w.length := by simpa using hi
      simp [Word.pow_one, hi', Nat.mod_eq_of_lt hi']
    · intro i hi
      rw [Word.pow_succ w (Nat.succ k)]
      have hlen : (w ^ (Nat.succ k)).length = (Nat.succ k) * w.length := Word.length_pow w (Nat.succ k)
```

--- Planning Phase (Iteration 3/3) ---

[PlannerAgent] Reasoning:
We need to prove `HasPeriod (w^(n+1)) w.length` under the assumption `hw : w ≠ []`. The period condition requires `0 < w.length` (immediate from `hw` via `List.length_pos_iff_ne_nil`) and for all indices `i` with `i + w.length < (w^(n+1)).length`, the entries at `i` and `i+w.length` are equal. The key idea: in `w^(n+1)`, the value at any position `i` is entirely determined by `i % w.length` (the position inside the fundamental block `w`). This modularity lemma can be proved by induction on `n`. Then the main theorem follows by applying this lemma to both indices and using `Nat.add_mod_right`.

<plan>
### Step 1: Establish positivity of the period
- From `hw : w ≠ []` obtain `hpos : 0 < w.length` using `List.length_pos_iff_ne_nil.mpr hw`.  
  This will be the first component of `HasPeriod`.

### Step 2: Prove a modular-access lemma by induction on `k`
- **Statement**: For any `k` and `i` with `i < (k+1)*w.length`,  
  `(w ^ (k+1)).get? i = w.get? (i % w.length)`.  

  Call this lemma `lemma pow_get?_mod (k i) (hi) : ... :=`  
  **Base case `k = 0`**:  
  - `w ^ 1 = w` by `Word.pow_one`.  
  - The hypothesis `hi` gives `i < w.length`.  
  - Then `i % w.length = i` by `Nat.mod_eq_of_lt hi`.  
  - The goal simplifies to `w.get? i = w.get? i` (done by `simp`).

  **Inductive step**: assume the lemma holds for `k`, prove it for `k+1`.  
  - Fix `i` and `hi : i < ((k+1)+1)*w.length` (i.e., `i < (k+2)*w.length`).  
  - Write `w ^ (k+2) = w ^ (k+1) ⬝ w` using `Word.pow_succ`.  
  - Let `h_len_pow : (w ^ (k+1)).length = (k+1)*w.length` by `Word.length_pow w (k+1)`.  
  - Perform a case split on `h_lt : i < (w ^ (k+1)).length`.  

    **Case 1** `h_lt` holds:  
      - The condition `h_lt` after rewriting with `h_len_pow` becomes `i < (k+1)*w.length`.  
      - Use `List.get?_append_left` (with `h_lt` rewritten) to obtain  
        `(w ^ (k+1) ⬝ w).get? i = (w ^ (k+1)).get? i`.  
      - Apply the induction hypothesis to the right‑hand side. This directly yields `w.get? (i % w.length)`.  

    **Case 2** `¬ h_lt`.  
      - From `¬ h_lt` and `hi` we deduce `(k+1)*w.length ≤ i` and `i < (k+2)*w.length`.  
        All arithmetic is handled by `omega`.  
      - Set `j := i - (k+1)*w.length`. Then `j < w.length` (by `omega`).  
      - Apply `List.get?_append_right` (using the inequality `(w ^ (k+1)).length ≤ i`, which follows from `¬ h_lt` and `h_len_pow`). The lemma gives  
        `(w ^ (k+1) ⬝ w).get? i = w.get? (i - (w ^ (k+1)).length)`.  
        Using `h_len_pow` this rewrites to `w.get? j`.  
      - We still need to show `w.get? j = w.get? (i % w.length)`.  
        Observe that `i = (k+1)*w.length + j` (by `omega`) and `j < w.length`.  
        Therefore `i % w.length = j % w.length = j` (the last equality by `Nat.mod_eq_of_lt` because `j < w.length`).  
        `omega` can prove the entire arithmetic equality; we can simply `omega` at this point to close the goal.

### Step 3: Apply the modular lemma to the main period condition
- Let `h_pow_len : (w ^ (n+1)).length = (n+1)*w.length` by `Word.length_pow w (n+1)`.
- The second component of `HasPeriod` requires showing:  
  for any `i`, if `i + w.length < (w ^ (n+1)).length` then `(w ^ (n+1)).get? i = (w ^ (n+1)).get? (i + w.length)`.
- Take an arbitrary `i` and `hi`.  
  Rewrite `hi` with `h_pow_len` to obtain `hi' : i + w.length < (n+1)*w.length`.  
- From `hi'` we immediately have `hi_i : i < (n+1)*w.length` and `hi_ip : i + w.length < (n+1)*w.length` (both by `omega`).
- Apply `pow_get?_mod n i hi_i` to get `h1 : (w ^ (n+1)).get? i = w.get? (i % w.length)`.
- Apply `pow_get?_mod n (i+w.length) hi_ip` to get `h2 : (w ^ (n+1)).get? (i+w.length) = w.get? ((i+w.length) % w.length)`.
- By the lemma `Nat.add_mod_right` (or `Nat.add_mod`), we have `(i + w.length) % w.length = i % w.length`.  
  This can be finished with `simp [Nat.add_mod_right]` or by `rw` of the lemma.
- The two right‑hand sides become equal, hence the total equality holds.

### Step 4: Assemble the final result
- `refine ⟨hpos, λ i hi => ?_⟩` and then provide the chain of equalities from Step 3.

### Key lemmas used
- `List.length_pos_iff_ne_nil`
- `Word.pow_one`, `Word.pow_succ`, `Word.length_pow` (from the CoW library)
- `List.get?_append_left`, `List.get?_append_right` (Mathlib `List` API)
- `Nat.mod_eq_of_lt`, `Nat.add_mod_right` (Mathlib `Nat` API)
- `omega` tactic for all arithmetic inequalities and equality reasoning.
</plan>

[PlannerAgent] Plan:
### Step 1: Establish positivity of the period
- From `hw : w ≠ []` obtain `hpos : 0 < w.length` using `List.length_pos_iff_ne_nil.mpr hw`.  
  This will be the first component of `HasPeriod`.

### Step 2: Prove a modular-access lemma by induction on `k`
- **Statement**: For any `k` and `i` with `i < (k+1)*w.length`,  
  `(w ^ (k+1)).get? i = w.get? (i % w.length)`.  

  Call this lemma `lemma pow_get?_mod (k i) (hi) : ... :=`  
  **Base case `k = 0`**:  
  - `w ^ 1 = w` by `Word.pow_one`.  
  - The hypothesis `hi` gives `i < w.length`.  
  - Then `i % w.length = i` by `Nat.mod_eq_of_lt hi`.  
  - The goal simplifies to `w.get? i = w.get? i` (done by `simp`).

  **Inductive step**: assume the lemma holds for `k`, prove it for `k+1`.  
  - Fix `i` and `hi : i < ((k+1)+1)*w.length` (i.e., `i < (k+2)*w.length`).  
  - Write `w ^ (k+2) = w ^ (k+1) ⬝ w` using `Word.pow_succ`.  
  - Let `h_len_pow : (w ^ (k+1)).length = (k+1)*w.length` by `Word.length_pow w (k+1)`.  
  - Perform a case split on `h_lt : i < (w ^ (k+1)).length`.  

    **Case 1** `h_lt` holds:  
      - The condition `h_lt` after rewriting with `h_len_pow` becomes `i < (k+1)*w.length`.  
      - Use `List.get?_append_left` (with `h_lt` rewritten) to obtain  
        `(w ^ (k+1) ⬝ w).get? i = (w ^ (k+1)).get? i`.  
      - Apply the induction hypothesis to the right‑hand side. This directly yields `w.get? (i % w.length)`.  

    **Case 2** `¬ h_lt`.  
      - From `¬ h_lt` and `hi` we deduce `(k+1)*w.length ≤ i` and `i < (k+2)*w.length`.  
        All arithmetic is handled by `omega`.  
      - Set `j := i - (k+1)*w.length`. Then `j < w.length` (by `omega`).  
      - Apply `List.get?_append_right` (using the inequality `(w ^ (k+1)).length ≤ i`, which follows from `¬ h_lt` and `h_len_pow`). The lemma gives  
        `(w ^ (k+1) ⬝ w).get? i = w.get? (i - (w ^ (k+1)).length)`.  
        Using `h_len_pow` this rewrites to `w.get? j`.  
      - We still need to show `w.get? j = w.get? (i % w.length)`.  
        Observe that `i = (k+1)*w.length + j` (by `omega`) and `j < w.length`.  
        Therefore `i % w.length = j % w.length = j` (the last equality by `Nat.mod_eq_of_lt` because `j < w.length`).  
        `omega` can prove the entire arithmetic equality; we can simply `omega` at this point to close the goal.

### Step 3: Apply the modular lemma to the main period condition
- Let `h_pow_len : (w ^ (n+1)).length = (n+1)*w.length` by `Word.length_pow w (n+1)`.
- The second component of `HasPeriod` requires showing:  
  for any `i`, if `i + w.length < (w ^ (n+1)).length` then `(w ^ (n+1)).get? i = (w ^ (n+1)).get? (i + w.length)`.
- Take an arbitrary `i` and `hi`.  
  Rewrite `hi` with `h_pow_len` to obtain `hi' : i + w.length < (n+1)*w.length`.  
- From `hi'` we immediately have `hi_i : i < (n+1)*w.length` and `hi_ip : i + w.length < (n+1)*w.length` (both by `omega`).
- Apply `pow_get?_mod n i hi_i` to get `h1 : (w ^ (n+1)).get? i = w.get? (i % w.length)`.
- Apply `pow_get?_mod n (i+w.length) hi_ip` to get `h2 : (w ^ (n+1)).get? (i+w.length) = w.get? ((i+w.length) % w.length)`.
- By the lemma `Nat.add_mod_right` (or `Nat.add_mod`), we have `(i + w.length) % w.length = i % w.length`.  
  This can be finished with `simp [Nat.add_mod_right]` or by `rw` of the lemma.
- The two right‑hand sides become equal, hence the total equality holds.

### Step 4: Assemble the final result
- `refine ⟨hpos, λ i hi => ?_⟩` and then provide the chain of equalities from Step 3.

### Key lemmas used
- `List.length_pos_iff_ne_nil`
- `Word.pow_one`, `Word.pow_succ`, `Word.length_pow` (from the CoW library)
- `List.get?_append_left`, `List.get?_append_right` (Mathlib `List` API)
- `Nat.mod_eq_of_lt`, `Nat.add_mod_right` (Mathlib `Nat` API)
- `omega` tactic for all arithmetic inequalities and equality reasoning.

- `rw [applyMorphism f (a :: u), applyMorphism f u]`  
  This turns the goal into  
  `(List.flatMap f (a :: u)).length = (f a).length + (List.flatMap f u).length`.

### Step 2: Apply `List.flatMap_cons`
- The lemma `List.flatMap_cons` states: `List.flatMap f (a :: l) = f a ++ List.flatMap f l`.
- `rw [List.flatMap_cons f a u]` replaces the left‑hand side with `(f a ++ List.flatMap f u).length`.
- The goal is now:  
  `(f a ++ List.flatMap f u).length = (f a).length + (List.flatMap f u).length`.

### Step 3: Apply `List.length_append`
- The lemma `List.length_append` gives the length of an append as the sum of the lengths.
- `rw [List.length_append (f a) (List.flatMap f u)]` turns the left‑hand side into exactly the right‑hand side.

### Step 4: Conclude
- After these rewrites, the goal is an identity. The proof is complete.

- `applyMorphism` (definition from the CoW library)
- `List.flatMap_cons` (from Mathlib/Data/List/Basic)
- `List.length_append` (from Mathlib/Data/List/Basic)
</plan>

[43/45]       Morphism |   HARD | morphism_preserves_proper_prefix_ne

[Orchestrator] Initiating Multi-Agent Repair for morphism_preserves_proper_prefix_ne
[Orchestrator] Loaded CoW source context (26169 chars).

==================================================
--- Planning Phase (Iteration 1/3) ---

[PlannerAgent] Reasoning:
<plan>
### Step 1: Obtain the prefix part of the proper prefix
- From `h : u <ₚ w` we have `h.1 : u ≤ₚ w` (by `IsProperPrefix.isPrefix`).
- Apply the lemma `applyMorphism_preserves_prefix` from `CoW.Morphism` to get `h_pre_img : (f •w u) ≤ₚ (f •w w)`.

### Step 2: Decompose the proper prefix
- Using `IsProperPrefix.def` (from `CoW.ProperPrefix`) which gives `(u <ₚ w) ↔ ∃ v, w = u ++ v ∧ v ≠ []`.
- `rcases (IsProperPrefix.def u w).mp h with ⟨v, hw, hv_ne⟩`.
  Here `hw` gives the equality `w = u ++ v` (or `u ⬝ v`).

### Step 3: Express the image of `w` in terms of the images of `u` and `v`
- Apply `applyMorphism_concat` (from `CoW.Morphism`) to rewrite:
  `calc
    f •w w = f •w (u ⬝ v) := by rw [hw]
    _ = (f •w u) ⬝ (f •w v) := by rw [applyMorphism_concat f u v]
  `
  Call this equality `h_image`.

### Step 4: Prove that `f •w v` is non‑empty
- Because `hf : IsNonErasing f` says each letter maps to a non‑empty word, the image of any non‑empty word `v` is non‑empty.
- Perform a case analysis on `v`:
  - If `v = []`, contradiction with `hv_ne`.
  - If `v = b :: v'` for some `b : α` and `v' : Word α`, then
    `f •w v = f b ++ f •w v'` (by `simp [applyMorphism]`).
    The left term `f b` is non‑empty by `hf b`. Hence the whole concatenation is non‑empty by the lemma **`List.append_ne_nil_of_left_ne_nil`**.
- Name this fact `hv_img_ne : f •w v ≠ []`.

### Step 5: Show that `f •w u` is strictly shorter than `f •w w` (hence unequal)
- Suppose for contradiction that `f •w u = f •w w`.
- Substitute `h_image` to get `(f •w u) ⬝ (f •w v) = f •w u`.
- Take lengths on both sides using `Word.length_concat`:
  `(f •w u).length + (f •w v).length = (f •w u).length`.
- By `omega`, this forces `(f •w v).length = 0`.
- The lemma `List.length_eq_zero` (or `List.length_eq_zero.mp`) then yields `f •w v = []`, contradicting `hv_img_ne` from Step 4.
- Therefore `f •w u ≠ f •w w`.

### Step 6: Assemble `IsProperPrefix`
- The definition of `IsProperPrefix` is `u ≤ₚ w ∧ u ≠ w`.
- We already have `h_pre_img` from Step 1 and the inequality from Step 5.
- Conclude with `exact ⟨h_pre_img, inequality⟩`.

### Key lemmas used (exact names)
- `IsProperPrefix.isPrefix` (or `h.1` directly)
- `applyMorphism_preserves_prefix` (CoW.Morphism)
- `IsProperPrefix.def` (CoW.ProperPrefix)
- `applyMorphism_concat` (CoW.Morphism)
- `List.append_ne_nil_of_left_ne_nil` (Mathlib/Data/List/Basic)
- `Word.length_concat` (CoW.Word)
- `omega` tactic for arithmetic
- `List.length_eq_zero.mp` (Mathlib/Data/List/Basic)
</plan>

```lean4
have h_pre_img : (f •w u) ≤ₚ (f •w w) := applyMorphism_preserves_prefix h.1
  rcases (IsProperPrefix.def u w).mp h with ⟨v, hw, hv_ne⟩
  have h_image : f •w w = (f •w u) ⬝ (f •w v) := by
    calc
      f •w w = f •w (u ⬝ v) := by rw [hw]
      _ = (f •w u) ⬝ (f •w v) := by rw [applyMorphism_concat f u v]
  have hv_img_ne : f •w v ≠ [] := by
    cases v with
    | nil => exact hv_ne rfl
    | cons b v' =>
      have hb_ne : f b ≠ [] := hf b
      have : f •w (b :: v') = f b ++ f •w v' := by
        simp [applyMorphism]
      rw [this]
      exact List.append_ne_nil_of_left_ne_nil hb_ne
  have h_ne : f •w u ≠ f •w w := by
    intro heq
    have h_eq_concat : (f •w u) ⬝ (f •w v) = f •w u := by
      rw [← h_image, heq]
    have h_len_eq := congr_arg Word.length h_eq_concat
    simp [Word.length_concat] at h_len_eq
    have h_len_v : (f •w v).length = 0 := by omega
    have hv_nil : f •w v = [] := List.length_eq_zero.mp h_len_v
    exact hv_img_ne hv_nil
  exact ⟨h_pre_img, h_ne⟩
```

```lean4
  have h_pre_img : (f •w u) ≤ₚ (f •w w) := by
    rw [hw, applyMorphism_concat f u v]
    apply (IsPrefix.def _ _).mpr
    exact ⟨f •w v, rfl⟩
  have hv_img_ne : f •w v ≠ [] := by
    induction v with
    | nil => exact hv_ne rfl
    | cons b v' ih =>
      rw [applyMorphism, List.flatMap_cons]
      exact List.append_ne_nil_of_left_ne_nil (hf b)
  have h_ne : f •w u ≠ f •w w := by
    intro heq
    have h_eq_concat : (f •w u) ⬝ (f •w v) = f •w u := by
      calc
        (f •w u) ⬝ (f •w v) = f •w (u ⬝ v) := by rw [← applyMorphism_concat f u v]
        _ = f •w w := by rw [← hw]
        _ = f •w u := by rw [heq]
    have h_len_eq := congr_arg Word.length h_eq_concat
    rw [Word.length_concat] at h_len_eq
    have h_len_v : (f •w v).length = 0 := by omega
    have hv_nil : f •w v = [] := List.length_eq_zero.mp h_len_v
    exact hv_img_ne hv_nil
  exact ⟨h_pre_img, h_ne⟩
```

```lean4
rcases (IsProperPrefix.def u w).mp h with ⟨v, hw, hv_ne⟩
  have h_pre_img : (f •w u) ≤ₚ (f •w w) := by
    rw [hw, applyMorphism_concat f u v]
    exact (IsPrefix.def _ _).mpr ⟨f •w v, rfl⟩
  have hv_img_ne : f •w v ≠ [] := by
    match v with
    | [] => exact hv_ne rfl
    | b :: v' =>
      have h_eq : f •w (b :: v') = f b ⬝ f •w v' := by
        calc
          f •w (b :: v') = f •w (Word.letter b ⬝ v') := rfl
          _ = (f •w Word.letter b) ⬝ (f •w v') := by rw [applyMorphism_concat]
          _ = f b ⬝ (f •w v') := by rw [applyMorphism_letter]
      rw [h_eq]
      intro hnil
      have hb_nil : f b = [] := (List.append_eq_nil.mp hnil).1
      exact hf b hb_nil
  have h_ne : f •w u ≠ f •w w := by
    intro heq
    have h_concat : (f •w u) ⬝ (f •w v) = f •w u := by
      rw [← applyMorphism_concat, ← hw, heq]
    have h_len_eq := congr_arg Word.length h_concat
    rw [Word.length_concat] at h_len_eq
    have h_len_v : (f •w v).length = 0 := by
      apply Nat.add_right_cancel (a := (f •w u).length) (b := (f •w v).length) (c := 0)
      simpa [add_zero] using h_len_eq
    have hv_nil : f •w v = [] := List.length_eq_zero.mp h_len_v
    exact hv_img_ne hv_nil
  exact ⟨h_pre_img, h_ne⟩
```

[PlannerAgent] Reasoning:
<plan>
### Step 1: Extract the prefix part
- From `h : u <ₚ w`, we have `h.1 : u ≤ₚ w` (by `IsProperPrefix.isPrefix`).

### Step 2: Show the image is a prefix
- Use lemma `applyMorphism_preserves_prefix` (from `CoW.Morphism`) with `h.1` to obtain `h_pre_img : (f •w u) ≤ₚ (f •w w)`.

### Step 3: Decompose the proper prefix
- Use `IsProperPrefix.def` (from `CoW.ProperPrefix`) to get `∃ v, w = u ++ v ∧ v ≠ []`.
- Let `⟨v, hw, hv_ne⟩` be that decomposition. Here `hw : w = u ++ v`.

### Step 4: Prove that the image of a non‑empty word is non‑empty under a non‑erasing morphism
- Show `hv_img_ne : f •w v ≠ []`.  
  Since `v ≠ []`, we can write `v` as `a :: v'`.  
  Then `f •w v = f •w (a :: v') = f a ++ (f •w v')` (by `simp [applyMorphism, List.flatMap_cons]`).  
  Because `hf : IsNonErasing f`, we have `hf a : f a ≠ []`.  
  The concatenation of a non‑empty list with any list is non‑empty; use lemma `List.append_ne_nil_of_left_ne_nil` (or `List.append_eq_nil` via contradiction).  
  So assume `f •w v = []`, then `f a ++ (f •w v') = []`, which forces `f a = []` (by `List.append_eq_nil.mp`), contradicting `hf a`. Therefore `hv_img_ne`.

### Step 5: Show the images are unequal
- Suppose for contradiction `heq : f •w u = f •w w`.
- Rewrite using `hw` and `applyMorphism_concat`:
  `calc
    f •w u = f •w w                   := heq
    _       = f •w (u ++ v)           := by rw [hw]
    _       = (f •w u) ⬝ (f •w v)     := by rw [applyMorphism_concat]
  `
  Thus we have the equation `(f •w u) ⬝ (f •w v) = f •w u`.
- Apply the left‑cancellation property of list concatenation:  
  Lemma `List.append_eq_self_iff` says `a ++ b = a ↔ b = []`.  
  So `(f •w u) ⬝ (f •w v) = f •w u ↔ (f •w v) = []`.  
  Hence we infer `h_empty : f •w v = []`.
- This contradicts `hv_img_ne`. Therefore `f •w u ≠ f •w w`.

### Step 6: Combine into `IsProperPrefix`
- The definition `IsProperPrefix` is `u ≤ₚ w ∧ u ≠ w`.
- We already have `h_pre_img` and the inequality.
- Return `⟨h_pre_img, inequality⟩`.

### Key lemmas used (exact names)
- `IsProperPrefix.isPrefix` (or `h.1`)
- `applyMorphism_preserves_prefix` (CoW.Morphism)
- `IsProperPrefix.def` (CoW.ProperPrefix)
- `applyMorphism_concat` (CoW.Morphism)
- `applyMorphism`, `List.flatMap_cons` (to expand on a `::` constructor)
- `List.append_ne_nil_of_left_ne_nil` (or `List.append_eq_nil.mp` for contradiction)
- `List.append_eq_self_iff` (or `by simp` — Mathlib's `simp` can prove `(l1 ++ l2 = l1) ↔ l2 = []`)
</plan>

--- Planning Phase (Iteration 3/3) ---

[PlannerAgent] Reasoning:
<plan>
### Step 1: Decompose the given proper prefix
- Use `IsProperPrefix.def` (from `CoW.ProperPrefix`) to extract the non‑empty suffix `v`:
  `rcases (IsProperPrefix.def u w).mp h with ⟨v, hw, hv_ne⟩`
  where `hw : w = u ⬝ v` and `hv_ne : v ≠ []`.

### Step 2: Prove that the image of a non‑empty word under a non‑erasing morphism is non‑empty
- Show `hv_img_ne : f •w v ≠ []`.
- **Proof by cases on `v`:**
  - `v = []` contradicts `hv_ne`.
  - `v = a :: v'` (for some `a : α` and `v' : Word α`):
    * `f •w (a :: v') = f a ++ f •w v'` by `simp [applyMorphism]`.
    * `hf a : f a ≠ []` (since `hf : IsNonErasing f`).
    * Lemma `List.append_ne_nil_of_left_ne_nil` then gives `f a ++ f •w v' ≠ []`. (Alternatively, `simpa` using `by simp [hf a]`).
- Hence `hv_img_ne` is proved.

### Step 3: Show the morphism images decompose similarly
- By `applyMorphism_concat` (from `CoW.Morphism`), we have `f •w (u ⬝ v) = (f •w u) ⬝ (f •w v)`.
- Together with `hw`, we get `f •w w = (f •w u) ⬝ (f •w v)`.

### Step 4: Reassemble as a proper prefix
- Apply `IsProperPrefix.def` in the forward direction:
  `(IsProperPrefix.def (f •w u) (f •w w)).mpr ⟨f •w v, ?_, hv_img_ne⟩`
  where the missing equality is exactly the one from Step 3.
- This gives `(f •w u) <ₚ (f •w w)`.

### Step 5: Write the final proof term
- Combine the above into a concise proof:
```
rcases (IsProperPrefix.def u w).mp h with ⟨v, hw, hv_ne⟩
have hv_img_ne : f •w v ≠ [] := by
  cases' v with a v'
  · exact hv_ne rfl
  · simp [applyMorphism, hf a]
refine (IsProperPrefix.def _ _).mpr ⟨f •w v, ?_, hv_img_ne⟩
calc
  f •w w = f •w (u ⬝ v) := by rw [hw]
  _ = (f •w u) ⬝ (f •w v) := by rw [applyMorphism_concat]
```

```lean4
    (IsPrefix.def _ _).mpr ⟨f •w v, h_eq⟩
  have h_ne : (f •w u) ≠ (f •w w) := by
    intro heq
    have h_concat : (f •w u) ⬝ (f •w v) = f •w u := by
      rw [← h_eq, heq]
    have hlen := congr_arg Word.length h_concat
    rw [Word.length_concat] at hlen
    have hlen_v : (f •w v).length = 0 := by omega
    have h_empty : f •w v = [] := List.length_eq_zero.mp hlen_v
    exact hv_img_ne h_empty
  exact ⟨h_pre, h_ne⟩
```

### Step 2: Prove that the image of a non-empty word under a non-erasing morphism is non-empty
- Show `hv_img_ne : f •w v ≠ []`.
- Since `hv_ne`, we can write `v` as `a :: v'` (by `cases v`).

  Let `h_image` be this equality.

### Step 4: Combine to form the border
- `IsBorder` is defined as the conjunction `b <ₚ w ∧ b <ₛ w`.  
  So `exact ⟨hpre, hsuf⟩` concludes the proof.

```lean4
have hf_ne : IsNonErasing f := hf.isNonErasing
  have h_len_image : ∀ (u : Word α), (f •w u).length = u.length := by
    intro u
    induction u with
    | nil => simp [applyMorphism]
    | cons a u ih =>
        simp [applyMorphism, List.flatMap_cons, List.flatMap_nil,
          List.length_append, hf a, ih]
  have hpre : (f •w b) <ₚ (f •w w) := by
    rcases (IsProperPrefix.def b w).mp hb.1 with ⟨v, hw, hv_ne⟩
    have hpos : 0 < (f •w v).length := by
      rw [h_len_image v]
      exact List.length_pos.mpr hv_ne
    refine ⟨?_, ?_⟩
    · apply (IsPrefix.def _ _).mpr
      refine ⟨f •w v, ?_⟩
      calc
        f •w w = f •w (b ++ v) := by rw [hw]
        _ = (f •w b) ⬝ (f •w v) := by simp [applyMorphism_concat]
    · intro heq
      have hlen_eq := congrArg Word.length heq
      have hlen_w : (f •w w).length = (f •w b).length + (f •w v).length := by
        rw [hw]
        simp [applyMorphism_concat, Word.concat, List.length_append]
      rw [hlen_w] at hlen_eq
      have hlen_eq' : (f •w b).length + (f •w v).length = (f •w b).length := by
        rw [← heq]
        exact hlen_w
      have hzero : (f •w v).length = 0 := by
        have : (f •w b).length + (f •w v).length = (f •w b).length + 0 := by
          simpa [Nat.add_zero] using hlen_eq'
        exact Nat.add_left_cancel this
      have : 0 < 0 := by simpa [hzero] using hpos
      exact Nat.lt_irrefl 0 this
  have hsuf : (f •w b) <ₛ (f •w w) := by
    rcases (IsProperSuffix.iff b w).mp hb.2 with ⟨u, hw, hu_ne⟩
    have hpos : 0 < (f •w u).length := by
      rw [h_len_image u]
      exact List.length_pos.mpr hu_ne
    refine ⟨?_, ?_⟩
    · apply (IsSuffix.def _ _).mpr
      refine ⟨f •w u, ?_⟩

      have hlen_eq' : (f •w u).length + (f •w b).length = (f •w b).length := by
        rw [← heq]
        exact hlen_w
      have hzero : (f •w u).length = 0 := by
        have : (f •w u).length + (f •w b).length = 0 + (f •w b).length := by
          simpa [Nat.zero_add] using hlen_eq'
        exact Nat.add_right_cancel this
      have : 0 < 0 := by simpa [hzero] using hpos
      exact Nat.lt_irrefl 0 this
```

### Step 2: Length preservation for the morphism
- From `h_uniform` we have `IsUniform.length_image h_uniform u` giving `(f •w u).length = u.length * 1`.  
  Simplify the right‑hand side using `Nat.one_mul` (or `mul_comm` and `mul_one`) to get `(f •w u).length = u.length`.  
- So we can derive a helper lemma `h_len (u : Word α) : (f •w u).length = u.length`.

### Step 3: Prove `(f •w b) <ₚ (f •w w)`
- From `hb.1 : IsProperPrefix b w` we have `hb_pre : b ≤ₚ w := hb.1.1` and `hb_ne : b ≠ w` is already implied by properness, but more useful is `hb.1.length_lt : b.length < w.length`.
- Use `applyMorphism_preserves_prefix hb_pre` (lemma from `CoW/Morphism`) to get `h_pre_img : (f •w b) ≤ₚ (f •w w)`.
- For the inequality: suppose `heq : (f •w b) = (f •w w)`.  
  `have hlen_eq := congrArg Word.length heq`; rewrite both sides with `h_len` to get `b.length = w.length`.  
  This contradicts `hb.1.length_lt` because `b.length < w.length`. Hence `(f •w b) ≠ (f •w w)`.
- Return `⟨h_pre_img, by intro heq; apply (Nat.ne_of_lt hb.1.length_lt) (by ...)⟩`.
